Salah — Prayer

Exceptions to the Captive Child Ruling
Lists three exceptions where a captive child is considered Muslim and deserves janazah prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi exceptions where a captive child is considered Muslim and apply the principle of khayr al-abawayn to determine eligibility for janazah.

Core Idea
A captive child is Muslim if a parent converts, the child converts, or captured alone.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a child captured with a kafir parent does not receive janazah prayer. However, Islamic law provides exceptions that acknowledge the child's potential for Islam. This lesson explores three specific scenarios where the child is considered Muslim and deserves funeral rites, supported by hadith and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Recall that a child captured with a kafir parent is not considered Muslim and does not receive janazah.
This baseline is essential to understand the exceptions.
2
Recognize the three exceptions
List the three scenarios from the passage: (1) one parent converts, (2) the child converts, (3) the child is captured alone.
Each exception has its own evidence.
3
Locate the evidence for each
For each exception, find the hadith or athar cited: Ibn Abbas for parent conversion, Jewish boy for child conversion, Hammad's athar for alone capture.
Also note the fitrah hadith as a general principle.
4
Understand the underlying principles
The child follows the better parent (khayr al-abawayn); the child's own conversion is valid; dar al-Islam defaults to Islam.
These principles guide the exceptions.
5
Apply the exceptions
Given a scenario, determine which exception applies and whether janazah is prayed.
Practice with hypothetical cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۳۳) الا ان يسلّم احدهما او هو او لم يُسب احدهما معه

ترجمه : (۹۳۳) مگر یہ کہ ماں باپ میں سے ایک اسلام لے آئے ، یا بچہ خود اسلام لائے ، یا والدین میں سے کوئی بچے کے ساتھ قید نہ ہوا ہو۔ [ تو نماز پڑھی جائے گی ]

تشریح : یہاں تین صورتیں ہیں [1] پہلی صورت ہے کہ ماں باپ میں سے کوئی ایک مسلمان ہو جائے تو افضل دین کے تابع بنا کر بچے کو مسلمان سمجھا جائے گا، اور نماز پڑھی جائے گی ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ بچہ سمجھ دار ہواور وہ خود مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی ۔ [۳] تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ماں باپ میں سے کوئی قید نہ ہوا ہو تو دار الاسلام ہونے کی وجہ سے بچہ دارالاسلام کے تابع ہوکر مسلمان شمار کیا جائے گا اور نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔

وجه : (۱) اور بچہ خیر الا بوین کے تابع ہوتا ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ کسان ابن عباس مع أمه من المستضعفين و لم يكن مع ابيه على دين قومه ، و قال : الاسلام يعلو ولا يعلى - بخاری شریف، باب اذا اسلم الصمى فمات حل یصلی علیه ؟ ص ۲۱۶، نمبر ۱۳۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عباس کے والد حضرت عباس ابھی مسلمان نہیں ہوئے تھے وہ کافر تھے بعد میں مسلمان ہوئے ، اور اسکی والدہ مسلمان ہو چکی تھیں، تو حدیث میں حضرت ابن عباس کو ماں کے تابع کر کے مستضعفین کہا (۲) بچه خود مسلمان ہو جائے تو وہ مسلمان سمجھا جائے گا اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن أنس قال كان غلام يهودى يخدم النبي الله فمرض فأتاه النبي الا الله يعوده فقعد عند رأسه فقال له : أسلم ، فنظر الى أبيه و هو عنده فقال له أطع أبا القاسم علل الله فأسلم فخرج النبي الا الله و هو يقول : الحمد لله الذي أنقذه من النار . (بخارى شريف، باب اذا اسلم الصحى فمات حل یصلی علیہ؟ ، ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۱۳۵۴) اس حدیث میں یہودی کے بچے نے اسلام لا یا تو حضور نے اس کو قبول فرمایا۔(۳) اور تنہا بچہ قید ہو تو وہ دارالاسلام کے تابع ہو کر مسلمان سمجھا جائے گا۔ قال : و قال حماد : اذا ملكت الصبى فهو مسلم . (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلاۃ علی الصحی ، ج ثالث ص ۳۵۴ نمبر (۶۶۶ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسلمان آدمی بچے کا مالک ہوا تو بچہ مسلمان شمار کیا جائے گا۔ (۴) ہر بچہ اپنی فطرت کے اعتبار سے مسلمان پیدا ہوتا ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث اور آیت ہیں۔ عن ابا هريرة كان يحدث قال النبى الله ما من مولود الا يولد على الفطرة ، فأبواه يهودانه أو ينصرانه أو يـمـجـسـانـه .... ثم يقول ابو هريرة فطرت الله التي فطر الناس عليها . ( آیت ۳۰، سورة الروم۳۰)۔. ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا اسلم الصمى فمات حل یصلی علیہ؟ ، ص ۲۱۷، نمبر ۱۳۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر بچہ اسلام کی فطرت پر پیدا ہوتا ہے، اور آیت میں بھی اس کا اشارہ ہے۔

(۲) کا فر پر نماز جنازہ نہ پڑھنے کی ممانعت اس آیت میں ہے۔ ولا تصل على أحد مات أبدا و لا تقم على قبره انهم كفروا بالله و رسوله و ما توا و هم فاسقون - ( آیت ۸۴ ، سورۃ التوبۃ ۹)
(933) Except if one of them (the parents) accepts Islam, or he (the child) does, or one of them was not captured with him. Translation: Except if one of the parents becomes Muslim, or the child himself becomes Muslim, or one of the parents was not captured with the child. [Then prayer will be prayed.] Explanation: There are three scenarios: [1] The first scenario is that one of the parents becomes Muslim; then by following the better religion, the child will be considered Muslim, and prayer will be prayed. [2] The second scenario is that the child is discerning and he himself becomes Muslim; then prayer will be prayed over him. [3] The third scenario is that none of the parents was captured with him; then due to dar al-Islam, the child follows dar al-Islam and will be considered Muslim, and prayer will be prayed. Evidence: (1) A child follows the better of the parents; the proof is this hadith: ... (Ibn Abbas with his mother from the oppressed, and his father was not on the religion of his people...) (Bukhari, p.216) (2) If a child himself becomes Muslim, he is considered Muslim; the hadith of the Jewish boy who served the Prophet... (3) If a child is captured alone, he follows dar al-Islam and becomes Muslim; Hammad's statement: when you possess the child, he is Muslim. (4) Every child is born on fitrah; the hadith of Abu Huraira: every child is born on fitrah, then his parents make him Jew, Christian, or Magian; and the verse 'the fitrah of Allah upon which He created mankind'. (Bukhari) (2) The prohibition of praying janazah over a kafir is in this verse: 'And do not pray over any one of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave; indeed they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger and died while they were defiantly disobedient.' (Surah Tawbah 9:84)
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage provides the exceptions to the previous ruling. While the default for a child captured with a kafir parent is no janazah, three exceptions make the child eligible for Muslim funeral rites. First, if one parent converts to Islam, the child follows the better religion (Islam) and is considered Muslim. Second, if the child himself converts (and is discerning), he is a Muslim. Third, if the child was not captured with any parent (e.g., taken alone or with a non-parent), he is considered Muslim by virtue of being in dar al-Islam. The author supports each exception with evidence: (1) the hadith about Ibn Abbas being with his Muslim mother; (2) the hadith of the Jewish boy who accepted Islam at the Prophet's invitation; (3) Hammad's statement that a child possessed by a Muslim becomes Muslim; (4) the universal principle that every child is born on fitrah (Islam), indicating that the default is Islam. The passage also reinforces the prohibition of janazah on kafirs with the Quranic verse (9:84). The Hanafi school uses these exceptions to balance the general rule and ensure that wherever Islam is the likely or chosen path, the child receives proper rites.

Key Terms
خير الأبوين (khayr al-abawayn): The better of the two parents in terms of religion; the child follows the parent with the superior religion (Islam over kufr).
دار الإسلام (dar al-islam): Territory governed by Islamic law; a child in dar al-islam without a kafir parent is considered Muslim.
فطرة (fitrah): The innate disposition towards Islam; every child is born upon the fitrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the exceptions mentioned in this passage where a captive child receives janazah prayer?
A) One parent accepts Islam.
B) The child himself accepts Islam.
C) The child is captured alone without any parent.
D) The child is captured with both parents but they are Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A captive child is considered Muslim for janazah if a parent converts, the child converts, or the child is captured alone.

Funeral Prayer for a Child of Mixed-Religion Parents: Three Scenarios
Explains three scenarios for funeral prayer over a child with one Muslim parent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi scenarios in which a child of mixed-religion parents is considered Muslim for funeral prayer and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
A child follows the better religion of the parents; three scenarios trigger funeral prayer.

When a child has one Muslim parent, questions arise about the child's religious status for funeral purposes. This passage from Thamaratun Najah clarifies three situations in which the Hanafi school considers the child Muslim and thus wajib to pray over. The author provides prophetic hadith and other proofs to support each scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three cases where the child is considered Muslim: (1) one parent accepts Islam, (2) the child himself becomes Muslim if discerning, (3) neither parent is bound (child in Dar al-Islam).
The third scenario applies when the child is not legally attached to the non-Muslim parent's religion.
2
Locate the evidence for each scenario
For each scenario, find the hadith or athar cited by the author: (1) hadith of Ibn Abbas, (2) hadith of the Jewish boy, (3) athar of Hammad and the fitrah hadith.
The fitrah hadith supports all scenarios by stating every child is born Muslim.
3
Explain how the evidence proves the ruling
Connect each evidence to the Hanafi principle that the child follows the better religion or is Muslim by virtue of Dar al-Islam. The phrase 'with his mother among the oppressed' shows the child follows the Muslim mother.
The hadith 'Islam is high and nothing is higher' reinforces the precedence of Islam.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Other schools may differ on the criteria. For example, the Shafi'i school may consider the child to follow the father's religion. This explains why the Hanafi school provides explicit proofs for its position.
The passage does not detail the opposing view but references the principle 'Islam is high'.

وجه : (۱) اور بچہ خیر الا بوین کے تابع ہوتا ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ کسان ابن عباس مع أمه من المستضعفين و لم يكن مع ابيه على دين قومه ، و قال : الاسلام يعلو ولا يعلى - بخاری شریف، باب اذا اسلم الصمى فمات حل یصلی علیه ؟ ص ۲۱۶، نمبر ۱۳۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عباس کے والد حضرت عباس ابھی مسلمان نہیں ہوئے تھے وہ کافر تھے بعد میں مسلمان ہوئے ، اور اسکی والدہ مسلمان ہو چکی تھیں، تو حدیث میں حضرت ابن عباس کو ماں کے تابع کر کے مستضعفین کہا (۲) بچه خود مسلمان ہو جائے تو وہ مسلمان سمجھا جائے گا اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن أنس قال كان غلام يهودى يخدم النبي الله فمرض فأتاه النبي الا الله يعوده فقعد عند رأسه فقال له : أسلم ، فنظر الى أبيه و هو عنده فقال له أطع أبا القاسم علل الله فأسلم فخرج النبي الا الله و هو يقول : الحمد لله الذي أنقذه من النار . (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلاۃ علی الصحی ، ج ثالث ص ۳۵۴ نمبر (۶۶۶ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسلمان آدمی بچے کا مالک ہوا تو بچہ مسلمان شمار کیا جائے گا۔ (۴) ہر بچہ اپنی فطرت کے اعتبار سے مسلمان پیدا ہوتا ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث اور آیت ہیں۔ عن ابا هريرة كان يحدث قال النبى الله ما من مولود الا يولد على الفطرة ، فأبواه يهودانه أو ينصرانه أو يـمـجـسـانـه .... ثم يقول ابو هريرة فطرت الله التي فطر الناس عليها . ( آیت ۳۰، سورة الروم۳۰)۔. ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا اسلم الصمى فمات حل یصلی علیہ؟ ، ص ۲۱۷، نمبر ۱۳۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر بچہ اسلام کی فطرت پر پیدا ہوتا ہے، اور آیت میں بھی اس کا اشارہ ہے۔
Chapter: Among them. (933) Except if one of them (the parents) accepts Islam, or the child himself, or one of them is not held (by the other's religion). (934) And if a non-Muslim has a Muslim relative, he will be considered Muslim. (2) The prohibition of offering funeral prayer over a disbeliever is in this verse: 'And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, nor stand at his grave; indeed they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger and died while they were defiantly disobedient.' (Surah at-Tawbah 9:84). Translation of (933): Except if one of the parents accepts Islam, or the child himself accepts Islam, or neither parent is bound (by the other's religion) [then funeral prayer is offered]. Explanation: There are three scenarios: 1) If one parent becomes Muslim, the child is considered Muslim according to the better religion, and prayer is offered; 2) If the child is discerning and himself becomes Muslim, prayer is offered; 3) If neither parent is bound, the child is considered Muslim by virtue of being in Dar al-Islam, and prayer is offered. Evidence: (1) The child follows the better of the two parents; the proof is the hadith: 'Ibn Abbas was with his mother among the oppressed and was not with his father upon his people's religion,' and he said: 'Islam is high and nothing is higher.' (Bukhari) ... (2) If the child himself becomes Muslim, the hadith of Anas about the Jewish boy who served the Prophet... (3) If the child alone is bound, he is considered Muslim by Dar al-Islam; the athar of Hammad: 'If a person owns a child, he is Muslim.' (4) Every child is born upon fitrah; the hadith of Abu Hurairah and the verse of Surah ar-Rum.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the ruling on offering funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) over a child from a mixed marriage where one parent is Muslim and the other is non-Muslim. The author presents three scenarios that result in the child being considered Muslim and thus entitled to funeral prayer: (1) one parent accepts Islam, (2) the child himself becomes Muslim if discerning, (3) neither parent is 'bound' (i.e., the child is not legally attached to the non-Muslim parent's religion). The text then provides four pieces of evidence from hadith and Quran: the first hadith establishes that a child follows the better religion of the parents; the second shows the Prophet accepting a Jewish boy's conversion; the third is an athar that a child owned by a Muslim is Muslim; the fourth is about fitrah. All proofs support the Hanafi position that funeral prayer is offered for such a child.

Key Terms
بچه خیر ابوین کے تابع (bachcha khayr al-abawayn ke tabi'): The child follows the better religion of the two parents; if one is Muslim, the child is considered Muslim.
دار الاسلام (dar al-islam): A territory under Muslim rule where Islamic law prevails. A child born here without binding to a non-Muslim parent is considered Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario is funeral prayer NOT offered over a child according to this passage?
A) When one parent becomes Muslim
B) When the child himself becomes Muslim
C) When neither parent is bound (i.e., no legal attachment to non-Muslim religion) and the child is in Dar al-Islam
D) When both parents remain non-Muslim and the child is an infant

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers funeral prayer for a child of mixed-religion parents in three scenarios: one parent converts, the child converts, or the child is unattached to the non-Muslim parent in Dar al-Islam.

Disposal of a Non-Muslim Relative's Corpse
Ruling on washing, shrouding, and burying a non‑Muslim relative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing and burying a non-Muslim relative and identify the proofs from Quran and Sunnah that prohibit Islamic rites.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim relative's corpse has no sanctity — wash it like a rag and bury without prayer.

When a Muslim's non-Muslim relative dies, a natural desire to honour the deceased may arise. However, Islamic law distinguishes between believers and others even in death. This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling that such a corpse is treated with minimal respect, deprived of the funeral prayer and full ghusl, based on clear scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The washing, shrouding, and burial of a non-Muslim relative. The ruling is permissibility (mubah), not obligation.
Note that the act is optional; the Muslim may also hand over the corpse to the deceased's own community.
2
Understand the minimal procedure
The corpse is washed like a filthy rag (i.e., without ritual ghusl), wrapped in a plain cloth, and placed directly into a pit. No funeral prayer is offered.
This contrasts sharply with the full Islamic burial rites for a Muslim.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet commanded him to bury his non-Muslim father without specifying any rites. This shows that a simple burial suffices.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood and is zanni al-thubut, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the Quranic prohibition of prayer
Surah at-Tawbah (9:84) explicitly forbids offering funeral prayer for disbelievers. This is a clear dalil for not performing salah over a non-Muslim corpse.
The verse was revealed about the hypocrites, but its 'illah is disbelief, covering all non-Muslims.

Source Text

فصل
غسله كغسل خرقة نجسة وكفنه في خرقة والقاه في حفرة او دفعه اهل ملته (۹۳۵) ولا يصلى على باغ وقاطع طريق قُتل في حالة المحاربة (۹۳۶) وقاتل بالخنق غِيلةً ومكابر في المصر ليلا بالسلاح ترجمه : (۹۳۴) اور اگر کسی کافر کا مسلمان رشتہ دار ہو تو اس کو ایک ناپاک کپڑے کی طرح دھولے اور ایک کپڑے میں کفن اور کا تو اور دے کر اس کو ایک گڑھے میں ڈال دے، یا اس کے اہل ملت کو دے دے۔ تشریح : کا فرشتہ دار کا انتقال ہوا، مثلا باپ کا انتقال ہوا تو چونکہ وہ کا فرمرا ہے اس لئے اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی اور اس کو مسلمان کی طرح کفن بھی نہیں دیا جائے گا، اور نہ مسلمان کی طرح غسل دیا جائے گا، البتہ ایک ناپاک کپڑے کی طرح دھولے اور ایک کپڑے میں لپیٹ کر گڑھے میں ڈال دے، یا جو اس کے کافر رشتہ دار ہوں انکو حوالہ کر دے۔
وجه : (1) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن على قال قلت للنبی الله الله ان عمك الشيخ الضال قد مات ، قال : اذهب فوار أباك ثم لا تحدثن شيئا حتى تأتيني . فذهبت فواريته و جئته فأمرني فاغتسلت و دعا لی . (ابو داود شریف ، باب الرجل یموت له قرابة مشرک ،ص ۴۶۹ نمبر ۳۲۱۴ رنسائی شریف، باب مواراة المشرک ،ص ۲۸۲، نمبر ۲۰۰۸) (۲) کا فر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی اس کے لئے آیت یہ ہے ۔ ولا تصل على أحد منهم مات أبدا و لا تقم على قبره انهم كفروا بالله و رسوله و ماتوا و هم فاسقون (آیت ۸۴ ، سورۃ التوبہ ۹) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کافر کی نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔ لغت خرقہ : کپڑے کا ٹکڑا ۔ حفرة گڑھا۔
Chapter: Its washing is like washing a filthy rag, and its shroud is in a rag, and throw it into a pit, or give it to the people of its religion. Translation of (934): And if a non-Muslim has a Muslim relative, then wash him like a filthy rag, and shroud him in a cloth, and put him in a pit, or give him to his co-religionists. Explanation: When a non-Muslim relative, e.g., father, dies, since he is a disbeliever, funeral prayer is not offered over him, nor is he given the Islamic shroud or bath. Rather, he is washed like a filthy rag, wrapped in a cloth, and buried in a pit, or handed over to his non-Muslim relatives. Evidence: (1) The hadith: 'Ali said: I said to the Prophet: Your uncle, the misguided old man, has died. He said: Go and bury your father, then do not do anything until you come to me. So I went and buried him, then came to him, and he ordered me to perform ghusl and prayed for me.' (Abu Dawood) (2) The verse prohibiting prayer over disbelievers: 'And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever...' (Surah at-Tawbah 9:84). Vocabulary: khirqa: a piece of cloth; hufra: a pit.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the treatment of a non-Muslim relative's corpse by a Muslim. The ruling states that the corpse is not given the full Islamic ritual bath (ghusl) but is simply washed like a filthy rag, wrapped in a plain cloth, and buried in a pit. Alternatively, it may be handed over to the deceased's non-Muslim community. The commentary clarifies that no funeral prayer is offered, and no Islamic shroud or bath is given. The proof includes the hadith of 'Ali about burying his father (who was non-Muslim) and the Quranic verse (9:84) prohibiting prayer over disbelievers. This reflects the Hanafi position that while a Muslim may handle the burial out of familial duty, the rites reserved for Muslims are not performed.

Key Terms
خرقة نجسة (khirqa najisa): A filthy rag; used to describe the minimal washing and wrapping of a non-Muslim corpse.
دفعه اهل ملته (daf'ahu ahl millatihi): Handing over the corpse to the deceased's own religious community for disposal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is given a ceremonial washing with water and camphor

Key Takeaway
A non-Muslim relative's corpse is washed minimally like a filthy rag, shrouded in a cloth, and buried without prayer, based on the Quranic prohibition and Prophetic practice.

Funeral Prayer Excluded for Rebels and Highway Robbers
Ruling on not offering funeral prayer over a rebel or highway robber killed during combat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on funeral prayer for a baghi and qati' tariq killed in combat, and explain the Hanafi evidence and rationale.

Core Idea
The imam withholds funeral prayer as a deterrent, but the deceased remains a Muslim and others may pray.

This lesson addresses a nuanced Hanafi ruling: while every Muslim deserves funeral prayer, there are exceptional cases where the Imam refrains as a disciplinary measure. Understanding this ruling clarifies that the absence of the Imam's participation does not negate the deceased's Islam nor the validity of prayer by others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and subjects
The act is funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The subjects are a rebel (baghi) killed during rebellion and a highway robber (qati' tariq) killed during robbery or confrontation.
Both are Muslims who died in a state of sin, but the ruling differentiates based on the manner of death.
2
State the hukm for the Imam
The Imam should not lead the funeral prayer over them. This is a prohibition based on deterrence (zajr wa tawrikh), classified as makruh tahrimi for the Imam.
The term 'makruh tahrimi' implies sin if done; it is not outright haram but strongly discouraged.
3
Understand the exception for others
Other Muslims may offer the funeral prayer without blame because the deceased is still a Muslim. The ruling only restrains the Imam.
This preserves the deceased's right to Muslim burial rites while achieving a larger societal goal.
4
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet did not lead the prayer over Ma'iz ibn Malik after his stoning for adultery, yet spoke well of him.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), so its evidence is zanni (probable) but accepted in Hanafi school for such rulings.
5
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of not leading the prayer while still affirming the man's goodness shows that the Imam may refrain as a deterrent without denying the deceased's Islamic status.
This analogy (qiyas) links the case of Ma'iz to rebels and highway robbers through the common illa of committing a major sin that warrants a deterrent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۳۵) ولا يصلى على باغ وقاطع طريق قُتل في حالة المحاربة
ترجمه : (۹۳۵) بغاوت کرنے والے پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی، اور ڈاکہ زن جو مقابلے میں مارا جائے اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
تشریح : جس نے حکومت عدل کے خلاف بغاوت کی اور مقابلے کے وقت مارا گیا، یا ڈاکہ زن ڈاکہ زنی کرتے وقت، یا مقابلے کے وقت مارا جائے تو جزر اور تواریخ کے طور پر اس پر امام نماز نہ پڑھے، باقی دوسرے لوگ پڑھ لے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ
مسلمان ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں حضور نے حد لگائے ہوئے پر نماز نہیں پڑھی . عن جابر بن عبد الله ان رجلا من اسلم جاء الى رسول الله..... فادرك فرجم حتى مات فقال له النبي الله خيرا ولم يصل عليه _(ابوداودشریف، باب رجم ماعز بن مالک ،ص ۶۲۳ نمبر ۴۴۳۰)
Translation of (935): And funeral prayer is not offered over a rebel and a highway robber killed in a state of combat. Translation of (935): Funeral prayer will not be offered over a rebel and a highway robber killed in combat. Explanation: One who rebelled against a just government and was killed at the time of battle, or a highway robber killed while highway robbery or in combat: the Imam should not offer funeral prayer over him as a deterrent and as a lesson. However, other people may pray; there is no harm because he is a Muslim. Evidence: (1) In this hadith, the Prophet did not pray over one who had been stoned for hadd. From Jabir ibn 'Abdillah: A man from Aslam came to the Messenger of Allah... he was caught and stoned until he died; the Prophet spoke well of him but did not pray over him. (Abu Dawood, bab rajm Ma'iz ibn Malik, no. 4430)
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It deals with the exclusion of funeral prayer for two categories of Muslims: those who rebel (baghi) against a just government and are killed during battle, and highway robbers (qati' tariq) killed during their crime or in combat. The ruling states that the Imam (ruler) should not lead the funeral prayer over them as a means of deterrence (zajr) and to set an example. However, other Muslims may pray for them without blame because the deceased is still a Muslim and has not left the fold of Islam. The proof cited is the hadith where the Prophet did not lead the funeral prayer over Ma'iz ibn Malik after his stoning for adultery, though he spoke well of him. This supports the principle that the imam may withhold prayer as a disciplinary measure while the deceased's Muslim status remains.

Key Terms
باغ (baghi): One who rebels against a just Islamic ruler; killed during combat.
قاطع طريق (qati' tariq): Highway robber or bandit; killed during robbery or in confrontation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Imam refraining from leading funeral prayer over rebels and highway robbers killed in combat is a deterrent measure, not a denial of their Islamic status; others may pray validly.

Funeral Prayer Excluded for Deceitful Killers and Night Attackers
Ruling on withholding funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories for whom the Hanafi school withholds the funeral prayer, explain the reasoning of deterrence, and identify that ghusl is still performed.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is withheld as a deterrent, not as excommunication – ghusl remains.

In this lesson, we examine a specific Hanafi ruling regarding funeral prayer. The text identifies three types of individuals for whom the imam does not lead the funeral prayer: one who kills by deceitful strangulation, one who uses weapons in the city at night, and one killed out of tribal prejudice. However, they are still washed (ghusl) as any Muslim. This ruling reflects a pedagogical deterrence, not a denial of Islamic identity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
List the three types mentioned: (1) one who kills by deceitful strangulation, (2) one who attacks in the city at night with a weapon, (3) one killed by tribal prejudice.
The common element is that the death involves blameworthy aggression or chaos.
2
State the ruling
For each category, funeral prayer is not offered by the imam. They are given a ritual bath (ghusl) but no prayer led by the community's leader.
The text explicitly says 'صلاة' is withheld, but ghusl is given.
3
Explain the reasoning
The Hanafi school withholds prayer as a deterrence (zajr) to discourage such heinous acts. It is not a denial of their Islam.
The deceased remains a Muslim; only the imam's congregational prayer is omitted.
4
Note what is still performed
Ghusl (ritual washing) is performed, and the body is still prepared as per Islamic rites, except the prayer.
This distinguishes from apostates or disbelievers who receive neither ghusl nor prayer.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) generally hold that every Muslim, regardless of sin, deserves funeral prayer. The Hanafi view restricts it for deterrence.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the performance of the prayer itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۳۶) وقاتل بالخنق غِيلةً ومكابر في المصر ليلا بالسلاح
ترجمه : (۹۳۶) اور فریب سے گلا گھونٹ کر مارنے والے پر ، اور رات میں شہر میں ہتھیار سے لڑائی کرنے والے پر ، اور تعصب کے مقتول پر نماز نہ پڑھی جاوے۔ ہاں غسل دیئے جائیں۔
تشریح : فریب اور دھوکا دیکر لوگوں کا گلا گھونٹ کر مارتا ہے، یارات میں شہر میں ہتھیار سے لوگوں کو مارتا ہے، یا قومی تعصب میں
Translation of (936): And one who kills by strangulation deceitfully, and one who attacks in the city at night with a weapon, and one killed by tribal prejudice: funeral prayer is not offered over them. Yes, they are washed. Explanation: He who kills people by deceit and strangulation, or he who attacks in the city at night with a weapon, or in tribal prejudice...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement without explicit proof in the given text. It addresses three categories of people for whom funeral prayer is not offered, though they are given a ritual bath (ghusl): (1) one who kills by deceitful strangulation (qatil bil-khanq ghilatan), (2) one who uses force (mukabir) in the city at night with a weapon, and (3) one killed by tribal prejudice (asabiyyah). The commentary explains that these are cases where the individual dies in a blameworthy manner, and the Imam refrains from offering funeral prayer as a deterrent. However, they are still Muslims and are washed. The text is incomplete, but the ruling aligns with the Hanafi position that certain categories of Muslims are denied the Imam's prayer for deterrence, though they remain within the fold of Islam.

Key Terms
قاتل بالخنق غيلة (qatil bil-khanq ghilatan): One who kills another by strangulation through deceit and treachery.
مكابر في المصر ليلا بالسلاح (mukabir fi al-misr laylan bil-silah): One who uses force and weapon in the city at night (i.e., committing robbery or assault).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer is withheld from deceitful killers and night attackers as a deterrent, but they still receive ghusl as Muslims.

Ruling on Funeral Prayer for Criminals Killed in Their Act
Ruling with proof: withholding funeral prayer from three categories of criminals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer for the three categories of criminals killed in their act and explain the proof from the hadith and analogy.

Core Idea
The imam withholds prayer from those who die in heinous crimes, but they remain Muslims deserving ghusl.

In the Hanafi school, not every Muslim who dies is automatically entitled to the imam's funeral prayer. This lesson addresses three specific cases where the imam refrains as a deterrent, yet the deceased are still given ghusl. Understanding this distinction sharpens our grasp of how the law balances mercy and justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories and the ruling
List the three types of criminals and note that the imam should not lead the janazah prayer for them.
The categories: (1) treacherous strangler, (2) one who fights in the city at night with weapons, (3) one killed in tribal partisanship.
2
Note the exception: they still receive ghusl
Recognize that these individuals are given the full ritual washing because they are Muslims.
Ghusl is obligatory for every deceased Muslim; the sin does not remove this right.
3
Examine the proof from the hadith of suicide
Read the hadith from Abu Dawood where the Prophet (ﷺ) refused to pray over a man who killed himself.
The hadith establishes that the imam may withhold prayer as a deterrent for grave sins.
4
Understand the qiyas (analogy) to the Prophet's action
Apply the same principle to the three categories: if the Prophet withheld prayer for suicide, it is even more appropriate for those who harm others.
The common factor (illah) is that the death occurred while committing a major sin.
5
Recognize the practical implication: the imam's role vs. others
Note that only the imam (or his deputy) refrains; other Muslims may pray if they wish.
This is a deterrent for the community, not a denial of Islamic brotherhood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۳۶) اور فریب سے گلا گھونٹ کر مارنے والے پر ، اور رات میں شہر میں ہتھیار سے لڑائی کرنے والے پر ، اور تعصب کے مقتول پر نماز نہ پڑھی جاوے۔ ہاں غسل دیئے جائیں۔ تشریح : فریب اور دھوکا دیکر لوگوں کا گلا گھونٹ کر مارتا ہے، یارات میں شہر میں ہتھیار سے لوگوں کو مارتا ہے، یا قومی تعصب میں لڑائی کر رہا ہے اور مارا گیا، تو ان لوگوں پر بھی جز رو تو شیخ کے طور نماز نہ پڑھے، البتہ غسل دیا جائے گا۔ دلیل اوپر کی حضرت ماعز والی حدیث ہے۔ حدثني جابر بن سمرة قال مرض رجل .... فانطلق الى النبي الله فاخبره انه قد مات قال و ما یدریک ؟ قال رأيته ينحر نفسه بمشاقص معه قال انت رأيته قال نعم قال اذا لا اصلی علیہ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الامام لا يصلى على من قتل نفسہ، ص ۴۶۵، نمبر ۳۱۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے خود کوقتل کیا اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی۔
Translation: (936) And upon the one who kills by strangulation treacherously, and upon the one who fights in the city at night with weapons, and upon the one killed for tribal partisanship, no prayer is performed. Yes, they are given ghusl. Explanation: He kills people by strangling with deceit and trickery, or he fights in the city at night with weapons, or he fights due to tribal partisanship and is killed. Upon these also, the imam should not pray as a deterrent, but they are given ghusl. Proof: The hadith of Ma'iz mentioned above. Jabir ibn Samurah narrated: A man fell ill... he went to the Prophet and informed him that he had died. He said: How do you know? He said: I saw him killing himself with arrowheads that he had. He said: Did you see him? He said: Yes. He said: Then I will not pray over him. (Abu Dawood, Sunan, book of the imam not praying over one who kills himself, p. 465, no. 3185) In this hadith, it is stated that whoever kills himself should not be prayed over.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The ruling: no funeral prayer is performed over three categories: (1) one who kills by strangulation treacherously (qatil bi al-khaniq ghilah), (2) one who fights in the city at night with weapons (mukabir fi al-misr laylan bi al-silah), and (3) one killed in tribal partisanship (maktul 'asabiyyah). However, they are still given ghusl. The explanation notes that these are people who die while committing serious crimes; the imam refrains from prayer as a deterrent, but since they are Muslims, ghusl is given. The proof cited is the hadith of the Prophet not praying over a man who committed suicide. The reasoning: if the Prophet withheld prayer from a suicide, it is even more fitting to withhold from these criminals who die while harming others. The hadith is from Jabir ibn Samurah. Note: The text uses the same hadith as used in the next lesson (937) regarding suicide; here it is applied analogically.

Key Terms
الخنق غيلة (al-khanq ghilah): Killing by strangulation through deceit and trickery.
مكابر في المصر ليلا بالسلاح (mukabir fi al-misr laylan bi al-silah): One who fights in the city at night with weapons, essentially a violent criminal.
عصبية (asabiyyah): Tribal partisanship or group fanaticism leading to fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) They are given ghusl, but the imam should not pray over them.
C) They are treated exactly like any other Muslim.
D) Only the imam prays over them, not others.

Key Takeaway
The imam's abstention from praying over these criminals is a deterrent, but they are still Muslims entitled to ghusl and optional prayer from others.

Suicide and Parent-Killer: Ghusl and Funeral Prayer
Distinct rulings for suicide and parent-killer funeral rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral rites for a suicide and a parent-killer, and distinguish the basis for each ruling.

Core Idea
Suicide does not remove Muslim status; parent-killer loses the right to funeral prayer.

This lesson compares two grave sins—suicide and killing a parent—and their consequences for funeral rites. The Hanafi school maintains that a suicide remains a Muslim and deserves ghusl and prayer, while a parent-killer, due to the enormity of his transgression, is denied the funeral prayer. We will explore the reasoning and underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases and their rulings
Read the matn: 'Qatilu nafsihi yughassalu wa yusalla 'alayhi, la 'ala qatili ahad abawayhi 'amdan.' Distinguish the ruling for suicide (washed and prayed over) and for parent-killer (not prayed over).
Note that ghusl is given in both cases; only the prayer is withheld for the parent-killer.
2
Understand the rationale in the explanation
The text explains: a suicide is a sinner (āthim) but not a tyrant (zālim), while a parent-killer is a tyrant. Hence the difference in prayer.
Tyranny (zulm) here refers to extreme transgression against parents, which is considered a much greater sin.
3
Locate the evidentiary basis
Though not quoted in this passage, the ruling for suicide is based on a hadith where the Prophet refrained from praying over a suicide, but the Hanafi school interprets that as the imam's personal act, not a universal prohibition. For the parent-killer, the proof is the principle of severe deterrence (zajr).
Refer to the previous lesson (hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah) for the suicide proof.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Many schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that a suicide should not be prayed over at all. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the imam refraining and the public praying, maintaining that the suicide remains a Muslim.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of interpreting prophetic actions as sunnah or personal preference, not wajib.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a case: a man kills himself in despair. Should the funeral prayer be performed? According to Hanafi, yes, the body is washed and prayed over, though the imam may choose not to lead. If a son kills his father in anger, then ghusl is given but no prayer.
The distinction remains based on the severity of the crime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقاتل نفسه يغسل ويصلى عليه لا على قاتل احد ابويه عمدا. ترجمه : (۹۳۷) اپنے آپ کو قتل کرنے والے کو نسل دیا جائے گا، اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی لیکن اپنے والدین میں۔ کسی ایک کو جان کر قتل کرنے والے پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ تشریح : اپنے آپ کو قتل کرنے والا گنہگار ہے لیکن ظالم نہیں ہے اور مسلمان ہے اس لئے نماز پڑھی جائے گی ۔ اور والدین کو قتل کرنے والا ظالم ہے اس لئے اس پر نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
And the one who kills himself is washed and prayed over, but not the one who kills one of his parents intentionally. Translation: (937) The one who kills himself will be given ghusl, and prayer will be performed over him. However, the one who kills one of his parents intentionally will not be prayed over. Explanation: The one who kills himself is a sinner but not a tyrant, and he is a Muslim, so prayer is performed over him. The one who kills a parent is a tyrant, so prayer is not performed over him.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This is a ruling with brief comparison. The Arabic matn states: 'Qatilu nafsihi yughassalu wa yusalla 'alayhi, la 'ala qatili ahad abawayhi 'amdan.' The explanation differentiates between the two: a suicide is a sinner but remains a Muslim; therefore, he is given ghusl and the funeral prayer is offered. In contrast, one who intentionally kills a parent is a tyrannical criminal (zalin); as a punishment and deterrent, the prayer is withheld. No separate proof is cited here; the proof was given in the previous lesson (the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah) where the Prophet refused to pray over a suicide, but here the ruling is opposite? Wait, that hadith says the Prophet did not pray over a suicide. This seems contradictory. The Hanafi position differs: they pray over the suicide because he is a Muslim, and the hadith is interpreted as the imam refraining as a deterrent, but others may pray. The text here explicitly says the suicide is prayed over. This is consistent with the Hanafi view that the imam may refrain but the general public may pray. However, the explanation in lesson 3 cited that same hadith for not praying over the criminals. There is a nuance: the imam may not pray, but others do. The explanation here says 'prayer is performed over him' without qualification, indicating the default. The parent-killer is not prayed over at all because his crime is greater. The proof for the parent-killer ruling is not given here but is based on the principle of deterrence and the severity of the sin.

Key Terms
قاتل نفسه (qatilu nafsihi): A person who commits suicide.
قاتل أحد أبويه عمدا (qatilu ahad abawayhi 'amdan): A person who intentionally kills one of his parents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The suicide is washed and prayed over; the parent-killer is not prayed over.
C) Both are washed and prayed over.
D) Neither is washed nor prayed over.

Key Takeaway
A suicide receives full funeral rites; a parent-killer is denied prayer but still given ghusl.

Sunnah of Four Men Carrying the Funeral Bier
Ruling with proof from hadith and companion practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of men carrying a funeral bier and identify the proof from hadith and companion practice.

Core Idea
It is sunnah for four men to carry the bier; more is permissible without blame.

This lesson examines the ruling on how many men should carry the funeral bier. The Hanafi school holds that four is recommended (sunnah), not obligatory. You will see the textual evidence from a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the example of Ibn 'Umar, and understand the practical flexibility allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is carrying the funeral bier (haml al-janazah). The ruling is 'yusannu' – it is sunnah (recommended). Look at the matn: 'Yusannu li-hamliha arba'atu rijal.'
Sunnah muakkadah in Hanafi means a highly recommended practice, omission of which is disliked but does not require compensation.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and a practice of Ibn 'Umar. Find the exact wording: Ibn Mas'ud says 'Falyahmil bijawanib al-sarir kulliha fa-inna min al-sunnah' – carrying all corners is from the sunnah.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah, no. 1478, and is classified as ahad (single-narrator) thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Understand the Hanafi position on number
The Hanafi position is that four is sunnah; more than four is permissible without being makruh. The explanation notes that if extra men help, there is no harm (la haraj).
This is based on the idea of balance: four corners are best, but additional carriers do not violate the sunnah.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools might require exactly four or treat it as obligatory. The Hanafi school views it as a sunnah, not wajib. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi reliance on the word 'sunnah' in the hadith is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۳۸) يسنُّ لحملها اربعة رجال فصل : في حملها ودفنها ترجمه : (۹۳۸) جنازہ کو اٹھانے کے لئے چار مرد مسنون ہیں۔ تشریح : جنازہ جس چار پائی پر رکھا جاتا ہے اس کا چار کو نہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے چار آدمی اٹھائیں گے تو چاروں کو نہ برابر ہوں گے، اس لئے چار آدمی مسنون ہے، اس سے زیادہ ہو جائیں تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ قال عبد الله بن مسعود من اتبع جنازة فليحمل بجوانب السرير كلها فانه من السنة ثم ان شاء فليتطوع و ان شاء فليدع ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی شهودالجنائزص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۴۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ چاروں پایوں کو پکڑ نا چاہئے اس لئے کہ وہ سنت ہے۔ (۲) اور قول صحابی میں ہے۔ رایت ابن عمر في جنازة فحملوا بجوانب السرير الاربع فبدأ بالميامن ثم تنحى عنها (مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۶۸ ، بای جوانب السرير مبداً فی اکمل ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۸۰ نمبر ۱۱۲۷۷/ مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب صفتہ حمل انعش ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۳۳، نمبر
(938) It is sunnah to carry it (the bier) with four men. Section: On carrying and burying it. Translation: (938) For carrying the funeral, four men are sunnah. Explanation: The bier on which the funeral is placed has four corners, so four men will carry it so that the four corners are balanced. Therefore, four men is sunnah. If more than that do it, there is no harm. Proof: (1) There is an indication in this hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: Whoever follows a funeral should carry all the corners of the bier, for that is from the sunnah; then if he wishes, he may volunteer, and if he wishes, he may leave.' (Ibn Majah, Sunan, chapter on attending funerals, p. 211, no. 1478) In this hadith, it is said that one should hold the four corners because it is sunnah. (2) And from the statement of a Companion: I saw Ibn 'Umar at a funeral, and they carried the four corners of the bier; he began with the right side then moved away. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on corners of the bier starting with the right, vol. 2, p. 480, no. 11277; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on description of carrying the bier, vol. 3, p. 1333, no. ...)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The Arabic matn states: 'Yusannu li-hamliha arba'atu rijal.' It is sunnah for four men to carry the funeral bier. The explanation notes that the bier (sarira) has four corners, so four men ensure balance; more men may participate without harm. The proof includes two sources: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud urging to carry all corners as sunnah, and the practice of Ibn 'Umar as a Companion precedent. This ruling is part of the new section (fasl) on carrying and burying the deceased. The Hanafi school emphasizes the sunnah aspect; it is not obligatory but recommended.

Key Terms
يسن (yusannu): It is sunnah (recommended, not obligatory).
حملها (hamluha): Carrying the bier (the funeral) on shoulders.
جنازة (janazah): Funeral bier or the deceased.

Key Takeaway
Four men carrying the bier is a sunnah practice; more are allowed without blame.

Undoing the Knot of the Shroud After Burial
Ruling on untying shroud knots after burial with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on untying shroud knots after burial and cite the evidence from Sunnah and athar.

Core Idea
Untying shroud knots after burial is sunnah — the reason for tying is gone.

When shrouding a deceased body, knots may be tied to prevent the shroud from opening during transport. However, once the body is placed in the grave, this risk no longer exists. The Hanafi school teaches that it is recommended (sunnah) to untie those knots. This lesson examines the evidence from hadith and athar that establishes this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its ruling
The passage rules that the knots of the shroud should be untied after burial. Determine the hukm level: fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.
The text uses a command form, but the context indicates recommendation.
2
Understand the rationale
Why were the knots tied initially? To prevent the shroud from opening during transport. After burial, that risk is gone, so untying is appropriate.
The change in circumstance is the key factor.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: one where the Prophet untied a knot with his mouth, and another instructing to untie the knots of the head and feet when placing the body in the niche.
The imperative 'أطلق' indicates recommendation in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i
A saying of the Tabi'i Ibrahim states all knots are undone when the deceased enters the grave.
This supports the practice.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that untying the knots after burial is sunnah. The proof is considered zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
Some scholars disagree, but the relied-upon view is to untie.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في حملها و دفنها (۹۴۹) وتُحلّ العقد ترجمه : (۹۴۹) اور گر ہیں کھول دی جائیں۔ تشریح کفن دیتے وقت کھلنے کا خطرہ ہو تو گرہ لگانے کے لئے کہا تھا۔ اب قبر میں میت کولٹانے کے بعد کفن کے گرہ کھول دے، اس لئے کہ اب کفن کھلنے کا خطرہ نہیں رہا۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ حـدثـنـا مـولاه معقل بن یسار لما وضع رسول الله الله نعيم بن مسعود في القبر نزع الأخلة بفيه - ( نمبر ۶۷۱۴)مـات ابـن لسمرة و ذكر الحديث قال : فقال : انطلق به الى حفرته فاذا وضعته في لحده فقل بسم الله و على سنة رسول الله الا الله ثم أطلق عقد رأسه و عقد رجليه ( سنن بیہقی ، باب عقد الا کفان عند خوف الانتشار وحلها اذا أدخلوه القمر ، ج ثالث ص ۵۷۱ نمبر ۶۷۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ گرہ کھول دے۔(۳) اس قول تابعی ہے۔عن ابراھیم قال اذا ادخل الميت القبر حل عنه العقد كلها (مصنف ابن ابى شیبه ۱۲۰، ما قالوا فی حل العقد عن المیت ، ج ثالث ص ۱۷، نمبر ۱۱۶۶۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفن کی گرہ کھول دی جائے۔
Section on carrying and burying her. (949) And he unties the knot. Translation: (949) And the knots are untied. Explanation: When giving the shroud, if there was a risk of it opening, it was said to tie a knot. Now, after placing the deceased in the grave, untie the knot of the shroud, because the risk of the shroud opening is gone. Evidence: (1) There is proof in this hadith: 'Narrated to us... Ma'qil ibn Yasar... when the Messenger of Allah placed Nu'aym ibn Mas'ud in the grave, he removed the knot with his mouth' (No. 6714). 'The son of Samurah died... he mentioned the hadith, he said: Go to his grave, when you place him in his niche, say: In the name of Allah and upon the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, then untie the knot of his head and the knot of his feet' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, section on tying the shrouds when fearing spreading and untying them when entering the grave, vol. 3, p. 571, no. 6715). This hadith indicates to untie the knot. (3) This is the saying of a Tabi'i: 'Ibrahim said: When the deceased is placed in the grave, all knots are undone for him' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 120, what they said about untying the knot from the deceased, vol. 3, p. 17, no. 11669). This athar shows that the knots of the shroud should be untied.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on untying the knots of the shroud after burial. The author states that after placing the deceased in the grave, the knots are untied because the reason for tying them—fear of the shroud opening during transport—no longer exists. Two proofs are provided: first, a hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi where the Prophet untied a knot with his mouth when burying Nu'aym ibn Mas'ud, and another hadith instructing to untie the knots of the head and feet after placing the body in the niche. Second, an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stating that all knots are undone when the deceased enters the grave. The ruling is that untying the knots is recommended (mandub) according to the Hanafi school.

Material for Lining the Grave: Mud Bricks and Bamboo Preferred
Ruling on using mud bricks and bamboo for covering the grave vs. baked bricks and wood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on grave lining materials and identify the proofs from the Sunna and the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Use perishable materials (mud bricks, bamboo) for grave lining; avoid permanent ones to hasten decay.

Funeral practices are governed by precise rulings rooted in the Sunna. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the material used to cover the grave niche (lahd). The source text contrasts sun-dried mud bricks and bamboo, which are recommended, with baked bricks and wood, which are disliked. The underlying rationale is to promote rapid decomposition, as decay is linked to divine mercy. Understanding this ruling helps avoid common cultural practices that may contravene the Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is lining the grave niche with material. The Hanafi ruling: using mud bricks (labin) and bamboo (qasab) is mustahab (recommended); using baked bricks (ajur) and wood (khashab) is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid but not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
Four evidences are cited: hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas instructing the use of mud bricks for his own grave; the report of Ali ibn Abi Talib about the Prophet's grave; the hadith forbidding plastering and building over graves; and the practice of the Salaf preferring perishable materials.
The primary evidence is the command to set up mud bricks (nasb al-labin) and the prohibition of building (bina') and plastering (tajsis).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command to use mud bricks indicates recommendation. The prohibition of building and plastering indicates dislike for permanent structures. The rationale (illa) is to hasten decay, as permanent materials prevent it.
The Prophet said: 'The grave should not be plastered, nor built upon, nor sat upon.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Some other schools allow baked bricks if there is a need (e.g., firm soil), but the Hanafi position emphasizes following the Sunna.
The Hanafi view is based on the practice of the Prophet and the Companions.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi tarjih relies on the zahir al-riwayah: mud bricks and bamboo are preferred; baked bricks and wood are disliked. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is to use perishable materials.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۵۰) قبر پر برابر رکھ دئے جائیں بیچی اینٹ اور بانس۔ اور مکروہ ہے پختہ اینٹ ، اورلکڑی۔ تشریح : تبر بوسیدہ ہونے کے لئے ہے، اور بوسیدہ قبر پر رحمت زیادہ اترتی ہے قبر کے اندر کچی اینٹ اور بانس سے منہ پاٹ دیا جائے ، اور اعلی قسم کی مضبوط سے پاٹن یا پکی اینٹ سے پاٹنا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اس سے قبر کو مضبوط کرتا ہے۔ وجه (۱) کچی اینٹ ڈالنے کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ ان سعد بن ابی وقاص قال في مرضه الذي هلك فيه الحدوا لي لحدا وانصبوا على اللين نصبا كما صنع برسول الله الا الله ( مسلم شریف، کتاب الجنائز، باب في اللحد ونصب اللين علی المیت ص ۳۸۹ نمبر ۲۲۴۰/۹۶۶) (۲) قال علی بن ابی طالب غسلت رسول الله الله ..... و لحد رسول الله له لحدا و نصب عليه اللبن نصبا - ( مستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب الجنائز ، ج اول ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۱۳۳۹) ان حدیثوں میں ہے کہ حضور کی قبر پر کچی اینٹ ڈالی گئی (۳) پکی اینٹ مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عـن جـابـر قال نھی رسول الله الله ان يـجـصـص الـقبـر وان يقعد عليه وان يبنى عليه ( مسلم شریف، کتاب الجنائز، فصل في النهي عن تخصيص القبور،ص ۱۳۸۹، نمبر ۲۲۴۵/۹۷۰/ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی البناء علی القبر ، ص۴۷۰، نمبر ۳۲۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبر پر پکی اینٹ اور تختہ نہ دیا جائے ، اس پر کوئی بنیاد نہ بنائی جائے، اور نہ چونے بیچ سے مضبوط کی جائے (۲)۔ عن ابراهیم قال كانوا يستحبون اللين و يكرهون الآجر ويستحبون القصب ويكرهون الخشب ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۳۷ ، في تجصیص القبر والآجر سبل لہ ج ثالث ص ۲۷ نمبر ۱۱۷۶۹) اس اثر سے بھی مسئلہ کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ لغت: اللبن: کچی اینٹ۔ الآجر : پکی اینٹ، خشب لکڑی، القصب: بانس۔
Translation: (950) On the grave, mud bricks and bamboo are placed evenly. And baked bricks and wood are disliked. Explanation: For quick decay, and decay brings more mercy. Inside the grave, the opening is sealed with mud bricks and bamboo. Using high-quality strong materials or baked bricks is disliked because it strengthens the grave. Evidence: (1) Hadith for mud bricks: Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died: 'Make a niche for me and set up mud bricks upon me as was done for the Messenger of Allah' (Muslim, Book of Funerals, chapter on niche and setting mud bricks, no. 2240/966). (2) Ali ibn Abi Talib said: 'I washed the Messenger of Allah... and a niche was made for him and mud bricks were set up' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, Book of Funerals, vol. 1, p. 515, no. 1339). (3) Baked bricks are disliked: Jabir said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade plastering graves, sitting on them, and building over them' (Muslim, no. 2245/970; Abu Dawud, no. 3225). (4) Athar: Ibrahim said: 'They used to prefer mud bricks and dislike baked bricks, prefer bamboo and dislike wood' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 11769). Vocabulary: al-labin: mud bricks; al-ajur: baked bricks; khashab: wood; al-qasab: bamboo.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the preferred materials for lining the grave. The author states that mud bricks (labin) and bamboo (qasab) are to be used, while baked bricks (ajur) and wood (khashab) are disliked (makruh). The reason is that the grave should decay quickly, as decay is a means of mercy. Using permanent materials strengthens the grave, which is contrary to the sunnah. Four proofs are given: hadith from Muslim showing the Prophet's grave was lined with mud bricks; a report from Ali; a hadith forbidding plastering and building over graves; and the practice of the salaf preferring perishable materials. The Hanafi ruling is that using baked bricks and wood is makruh tanzihan (disliked), and using mud bricks and bamboo is mustahab.

Key Terms
اللَّبِن (al-labin): sun-dried mud bricks, used for lining the grave
الآجُرّ (al-ajurr): baked or kiln-fired bricks
القَصَب (al-qasab): bamboo or reeds, used as covering material
الخَشَب (al-khashab): wood, used for coffin or covering

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using baked bricks (ajur) for lining the grave?
A) Sunnah
B) Mubah (permissible)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends mud bricks and bamboo for grave lining and considers baked bricks and wood makruh due to the prophetic command and practice.

Covering the Grave of a Woman vs. a Man
Ruling on covering the grave of a woman versus a man with proofs from athar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the grave of a woman versus a man and cite the evidence from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
A woman's grave is covered to preserve her modesty; a man's grave is not covered.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah in burial practices: covering the grave of a woman with a cloth while leaving a man's grave uncovered. The ruling is based on the principle of modesty ('awrah) and is supported by narrations from the Companions. Understanding this distinction helps ensure funeral rites align with the Hanafi school's emphasis on gender-appropriate dignity.

Guided Path
1
Name the act and its ruling
Identify the act (covering the grave with a cloth) and the ruling for men and women. According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah (recommended) to cover a woman's grave, but not a man's.
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib; omitting it is not sinful.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The author cites two athar (narrations from the Companions). The first indicates a covering was made for Fatima (RA); the second shows a cloth was removed from a man's grave by Abdullah ibn Yazid, who stated 'He is a man.'
These are qawl sahabi (Companion statements) and are considered evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the evidence for women
The hadith of Fatima (RA) describes a covering like the howdah of a bride, implying privacy and modesty. This establishes the practice for women.
The term 'hawdaj' emphasizes a dignified covering.
4
Analyze the evidence for men
The removal of the cloth from al-Harith's grave explicitly indicates that covering is not for men. The implication is that it remains for women.
The action of Abdullah ibn Yazid is a tacit approval from other Companions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a woman's grave is covered, a man's is not. Some schools may not differentiate; the Hanafi view is based on modesty considerations.
The ruling is a sunnah, not a strict obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب ۱۱۹، ما قالوا فی مد الثوب على القبر ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۷، نمبر ۱۱۶۶۳ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ستر الثوب على القمر ، ج ثالث ، ص ۳۲۳ نمبر ۶۵۰۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مرد کی قبر کو پردہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کی قبر کو پردہ کیا جائے گا
Thamaratun Najah, Volume 2, Section on Carrying and Burying Her. (951) And her grave is covered, not his grave. (952) And earth is thrown, and the grave is made like a camel's hump, and not made square. (953) And building upon it is forbidden. Translation: (951) And the grave of a woman should be covered; the grave of a man should not. Explanation: A woman used to live with covering in the world, so at the time of burial, it is better to cover her grave so that strangers do not see her. A man does not need that. Evidence: (1) Proof is in this athar: From Umm Ja'far that Fatima bint Rasulillah (may Allah bless him and give him peace) said: 'O Asma, I consider ugly what is done with women; a cloth is thrown over a woman and it describes her... This Khath'amiyah woman intervenes between me and the daughter of the Messenger of Allah? And I have made for her like the howdah of a bride?' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is reported about the bier for women, vol. 4, p. 56, no. 6930). This indicates that a covering like a hood is made for a woman. (2) Another athar: From Abu Ishaq: 'I witnessed the funeral of al-Harith, and they spread a cloth over his grave. Abdullah ibn Yazid removed it and said: He is a man.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on spreading cloth over the grave, vol. 3, p. 17, no. 11663; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on covering the grave with cloth, vol. 3, p. 323, no. 6503). This shows that a man's grave is not covered, and by implication, a woman's grave is covered.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on covering the grave of a woman but not a man. The author states that it is mustahab (recommended) to cover the grave of a woman with a cloth during burial to preserve her modesty, as she was veiled in life. A man's grave is not covered because there is no such need. Two proofs from athar are cited: the first shows that for Fatima (RA) a covering like a howdaj was made, indicating the practice for women; the second shows that a cloth was removed from a man's grave, indicating it is not done for men. The Hanafi position is that covering a woman's grave is mustahab.

Key Terms
سجى (sajā): to cover, especially the grave with a cloth
هودج (hawdaj): a covered litter or canopy used for women

C) To indicate it is a woman's grave
D) To follow a universal practice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling differentiates based on gender: a woman's grave is covered to maintain her modesty; a man's grave is not covered.

Shaping the Grave: Musannam (Raised) and Not Square
Ruling on heaping soil on the grave in a raised, hump-like shape and not making it square

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah shape of a grave according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice and hadith.

Core Idea
The grave is sunnah to be raised like a camel's hump (musannam), not flat or square.

This lesson deals with a simple but often misunderstood sunnah: the shape of the grave. You may have seen graves that are perfectly flat or very elaborate. The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's own grave and a clear hadith, teaches that the grave should be raised in a gentle hump. Let's examine the text and evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement: soil is thrown on the grave and it is made musannam (camel-hump-shaped), not square. Note that this is a sunnah act.
The Arabic term 'yusannam' literally means 'to make like a camel's hump'.
2
Understand 'Musannam'
Musannam means raised in the middle with sloping sides, like a camel's hump. It is not perfectly flat or square.
3
Examine the First Evidence
The writer cites Sufyan al-Tammar's report that the Prophet's own grave was musannam. This is a direct observation of the sunnah in practice.
Hadith from Bukhari and Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Examine the Second Evidence
The hadith of Ali commands leveling any 'elevated grave' (qabr mushtaf). This shows that only excessive height is prohibited, not a moderate hump. The Hanafi school reconciles both proofs.
Hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
5
Reconcile the Two Proofs
The first proof establishes the sunnah shape; the second places a limit: the grave should not be excessively raised. Together they define the musannam shape as a slight hump, about a handspan high.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۵۲) قبر پر مٹی ڈالی جائے اور کو ہان نما بنائی جائے اور چوکور نہ بنائی جائے۔ وجه : (۱) عن سفيان التمار ، أنه حدثه أنه رأى قبر النبي الله الله مسنما. (بخاری شریف، باب ما جاء فی قبر النبی وابوبکر وعمرص ۱۸۶ نمبر ۱۳۹۰/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۳۰، ما قالوافی القبر یسم ج ثالث ،ص ۲۳، نمبر۱۱۷۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ آپ کی قبر مبارک کو ہان نما ہے۔ (۲) قبر اونچی نہ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ قال لي على الا ابعثك على ما بعثنی عليه رسول الله الا اللهم ان لا تدع تمثالا إلا طمسته ولا قبرا مشرفا الاسويته . (مسلم شریف، کتاب الجنائز، فصل في طمس التمثال وتسوية القبر المشرف ص۳۱۲ نمبر ۲۲۴۳/۹۶۹ را بو داود شریف، باب فی تسویۃ القمر ، ص۴۷۰، نمبر ۳۲۱۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بہت ابھری ہوئی قبر کو نیچی کی جائے۔ لغت: کھال : مٹی ڈالی جائے پسنم : کو ہان نما بنائی جائے۔ سریع : چوکور، زمین کی سطح سے ملی ہوئی۔
Translation: (952) Soil is thrown on the grave, and it is made camel-hump-shaped (musannam), and not made square. Evidence: (1) From Sufyan al-Tammar that he saw the grave of the Prophet (may Allah bless him and give him peace) as musannam (camel-hump-shaped). (Bukhari, chapter on what came about the grave of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar, p. 186, no. 1390; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 11733). This shows that the blessed grave of the Prophet is hump-shaped. (2) That the grave should not be too high – the proof is this hadith: 'He said to me: Ali, I send you with what the Messenger of Allah sent me: Do not leave an image without obliterating it, nor an elevated grave without leveling it.' (Muslim, Book of Funerals, chapter on obliterating images and leveling elevated graves, no. 2243/969; Abu Dawud, chapter on leveling the grave, p. 470, no. 3218). This hadith indicates that a very raised grave should be lowered. Vocabulary: khal: soil is thrown; yusannam: made camel-hump-shaped; suray': square, level with the ground.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the shape of the grave. The author states that after burial, soil is thrown on the grave and it is made musannam – that is, raised like a camel's hump – and not made square or flat. Two proofs are given: first, a report from Sufyan al-Tammar that the Prophet's own grave was musannam. Second, a hadith instructing Ali to level any elevated grave, which implies that a slightly raised, hump-shaped grave is acceptable, but excessive elevation is prohibited. The Hanafi position is that the grave should be raised about a handspan or two, with a curved top, not flat or square. This is sunnah.

Key Terms
مسنم (musannam): shaped like a camel's hump, raised in the middle and sloping on sides
يربع (yurabba'): to make square or flat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What shape should the grave be made according to the sunnah?
A) Perfectly flat
B) Square and level
C) Raised like a camel's hump (musannam)
D) Very high and prominent

Key Takeaway
The sunnah grave is raised in a gentle hump (musannam), based on the Prophet's own grave and the command to level only excessively elevated graves.

Prohibition of Building on Graves
Ruling with proof on building over graves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building structures on graves, distinguishing between adornment (haram) and strength (makruh), and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Building on graves for adornment is haram; for strength it is makruh.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on construction over graves. The source text distinguishes between building for decoration (haram) and building for structural integrity (makruh). We will analyse the hadith evidence and the rationale behind the distinction, and clarify a common misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two rulings
The passage states that building on a grave is divided into two cases: if for adornment, it is haram; if for strength, it is makruh. Identify which case is forbidden and which is disliked.
Adornment includes decorative domes, tombs, or any beautification. Strength includes walls to prevent erosion or collapse.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah: the Prophet forbade plastering graves, sitting on them, and building over them. Identify the source and the key prohibition (nahi).
Hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud. The explicit prohibition (nahi) indicates haram in the Hanafi usul unless there is a specific reason to downgrade.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The nahi in the hadith normally indicates prohibition. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between adornment (haram) and strength (makruh) based on the rationale (illah) that graves are meant to decay quickly. Building for strength, though discouraged, is less severe.
The rationale: permanent construction prevents natural decay and wastes burial space.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
Some other schools allow building if it is not excessive. The Hanafi position is that even without adornment, it remains makruh and should be avoided.
The hadith is general, but Hanafi jurists use the illah to create the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۵۳) اور زینت کے لئے اس پر عمارت بنانا حرام ہے۔ اور دفن کے بعد مضبوطی کے لئے مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں دو باتیں ہیں [1] اگر قبر پر عمارت زینت کے لئے بناتا ہے تو حرام ہے ۔ [۲] اور زینت کے لئے نہیں بناتا بلکہ قبر کو مضبوط بنانے کے لئے بناتا ہے تو مکروہ ہے، اس لئے کہ قبر بوسیدہ ہونے کے لئے ہے، اور اس طرح کی تعمیر ہوتی رہے گی تو لوگوں کو قبر کی جگہ نہیں ملے گی ۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے . عن جابر قال نھی رسول الله علم ان يجصص القبر وان يقعد عليه وان يبنى عليه
Translation: (953) And building a structure on it for adornment is forbidden. And after burial for strength it is disliked. Explanation: Here there are two points: [1] If a building is erected on the grave for adornment, it is haram. [2] If it is not for adornment but to strengthen the grave, it is makruh, because the grave is meant to decay, and such construction will cause people to not get space for graves. Evidence: (1) In the hadith, Jabir said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade plastering the grave, sitting on it, and building upon it.'
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on building structures on graves. The author distinguishes two cases: building for adornment/decoration is haram (forbidden), while building for strength (without adornment) is makruh (disliked). The reason is that graves are meant to decay quickly, and permanent construction prevents that and wastes space. The hadith of Jabir (which also appeared earlier) forbids plastering, sitting on, and building over graves. The Hanafi ruling: building a dome, tomb, or any permanent structure for show is haram; if it is necessary to prevent erosion or animal disturbance, it may be permissible with conditions but generally discouraged.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): building a structure over the grave
يجصص (yujassisu): to plaster the grave

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone builds a decorative dome on a grave?
A) Sunnah
B) Mubah
C) Makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Building on graves for adornment is strictly forbidden (haram), while building for structural strength is disliked (makruh) based on the prophetic prohibition.

Writing on Graves: Permissibility and Proof Reconciliation
Permissibility of marking graves with writing to preserve identity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on writing on graves, identify the conflicting hadith, and explain the reconciliation between the permissive and prohibitive evidence.

Core Idea
Writing on graves is permissible for identification but disliked for adornment.

This lesson addresses a common question: can one write names or Quranic verses on a grave? The Hanafi school navigates between a hadith apparently forbidding writing and the Prophet's own act of marking a grave. We will examine the proofs and see how the school resolves the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
Read the opening statement: 'لا بأس بالكتابة عليه' (There is no harm in writing on it). Determine the hukm level from the term 'la ba's'.
In Hanafi fiqh, 'la ba's' indicates permissibility (mubah) or at least non-prohibition.
2
Locate the two sets of hadith
Identify the hadith that commands leveling elevated graves and the hadith where the Prophet marks a grave (permissive evidence), and the hadith forbidding writing on graves (prohibitive evidence).
The permissive hadith is from Abu Dawud; the prohibitive is from Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For each hadith, determine how it proves its ruling. The leveling hadith implies no monuments; the marking hadith proves identification is allowed; the forbidding hadith extends to writing.
The Hanafi school interprets the forbidding hadith as specific to adornment.
4
Reconcile the conflicting proofs
Apply the principle that the permissive proof (Prophet's action) is general, and the prohibitive proof is specific to writing for decoration. The prohibition is thus restricted to cases of adornment.
This reconciliation uses takhsis (specification) of the general command.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: for identification (e.g., a name plate) the ruling is mubah; for decorative calligraphy it is makruh tanzihi.
This distinction avoids the extreme of total prohibition or total freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بالكتابة عليه لئلا يذهب الاثر ولا يمتهن. قال لي علي بن ابي طالب الا ابعثك على ما بعثنى عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان لا تدع تمثالا الا طمسته ولا قبرا مشرفا الا سويته. (مسلم شريف، کتاب الجنائز، فصل في طمس التمثال وتسوية القبر المشرف ص ۳۸۹ نمبر ۲۲۲۳/۹۶۹ ابوداود شریف، باب فی تسویۃ القبر ، ص ۴۷۰، نمبر ۳۲۱۸). قال المطلب قال الذى يخبرني ذالك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال کانی انظر الی بیاض ذراعی رسول الله حين حسر عنهما ثم حملها فوضعها عند راسه و قال اتعلم بها قبر اخی و ادفن اليه من مات من اهلی. (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی جمع الموتی فی قبر والقبر يعلم ص ۴۶۸، نمبر ۳۲۰۶). نھی رسول الله ان تخصص القبور و ان يكتب عليها و ان يبنى و ان توطا. (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کراہیت تخصیص القبور و الكتابة علیها ،ص۲۵۴، نمبر ۱۰۵۲).
And there is no harm in writing on it so that the effect is not lost and it is not dishonored. Ali ibn Abi Talib said: I will send you as the Messenger of Allah sent me: do not leave any image without effacing it, nor any elevated grave without leveling it. Al-Muttalib said that the one who told me that from the Messenger of Allah said: I see the whiteness of the forearms of the Messenger of Allah as he uncovered them, then he carried it and placed it at his head and said: By this I know the grave of my brother and bury in it whoever dies from my family. The Messenger of Allah forbade plastering graves, writing on them, building on them, and trampling on them.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced ruling on writing on graves. The author first states that it is permissible (la ba's) to write on a grave for the purpose of identifying it (lā yadhhab al-athar) and to avoid disrespect (lā yumtahan). This permission is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who marked the grave of his brother (presumably 'Uthman ibn Maz'un) with a stone to recognize it, as reported in Abu Dawud. However, the author also cites a hadith forbidding writing on graves (naha an yuktaba 'alayha), which applies when the writing is for adornment and extravagance. The two rulings are reconciled by distinguishing between functional writing for identification (which is permissible) and decorative writing for show (which is makruh). The hadith of 'Ali (رضي الله عنه) about leveling elevated graves reinforces that graves should not be made into monuments. Thus, the Hanafi position is that writing for a legitimate need is mubah, but for adornment is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms
لا بأس (la ba's): Permissible; no legal objection.
يكره (yukrahu): Disliked; often denotes makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked).
تخصيص القبور (takhsis al-qubur): Plastering or making graves distinct with special construction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on writing on graves for the purpose of identification?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits writing on graves for identification based on the Prophet's practice, while prohibiting decorative writing based on the forbidding hadith, resolved by specifying the prohibition's scope.
