Ruling on Burying in Houses: A Prophetic Privilege
Burial inside houses is disliked except for prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on burial in houses, explain the prophetic privilege (ikhtisas), and identify the evidence from the Salaf.

Core Idea
Burial in houses is a special privilege for prophets—for others it is disliked.

The Hanafi school holds that burying the deceased inside a dwelling is makruh tanzihi for anyone other than a prophet. This ruling is rooted in the principle of ikhtisas (specific privilege) and is supported by the practice of the Sahaba. In this lesson, you will examine the two key narrations that establish this distinction and understand why what is honorable for prophets is not recommended for the general ummah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being judged? Burying a non-prophet in a house. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not haram). Note the reason: 'li ikhtisasihi bi'l-anbiya' (because it is specific to prophets).
Ikhtisas here means a legally recognized privilege exclusive to prophets.
2
Locate the dalil
Two pieces of evidence are cited: the athar of 'Umar (radi Allahu 'anhu) where a man is denied burial in a house and sent to the Muslim cemetery, and the hadith of 'A'isha (radi Allahu 'anha) regarding the Prophet's burial in his house.
Both are ahad (single-chain) narrations, so their thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar of 'Umar shows the normative practice of public cemeteries. The hadith of 'A'isha specifies that prophets are buried where they die, which is usually in their houses. The combination implies that household burial is a prophetic prerogative, not a general sunnah.
The Prophet's burial in his house was because it was the place of his death, not because it is recommended.
4
Understand the ikhtisas principle
Ikhtisas means a ruling that applies exclusively to a certain category. Here, burial in houses is an ikhtisas of the prophets. To imitate it without necessity is makruh tanzihi because it encroaches on a prophetic distinction.
The Hanafi school views such imitation as blameworthy (makruh) but not sinful (haram).
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa is that burial in houses is makruh for non-prophets. It may become permissible only in cases of genuine necessity, but the default is dislike.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالانبياء عليهم الصلوة والسلام. عن عمر بن ميمون قال جئت و اذا عمر واقف على حذيفة و عثمان بن حنيف ..... و ان لم تأذن فـردنـي الـى مقابر المسلمین. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ماجاء فی خلافة عمر بن الخطاب، ج سابع ص ۴۳۶، نمبر ۳۷۰۴۸). عن عائشة قالت لما قبض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اختلفوا في دفنه فقال ابو بكر سمعت من رسول الله شيئا ما نسيته قال ما قبض الله نبيا الا فى الموضع الذي يحب ان يدفن فيه فدفنوه في موضع فراشه. (ترندی شریف، باب این یدفن الانبیاء، ص ۲۴۶ نمبر ۱۰۱۸).
And burial in houses is disliked because it is specific to prophets, peace be upon them. From 'Umar ibn Maymun: I came and there was 'Umar standing with Hudhayfa and 'Uthman ibn Hunayf ... and if you do not permit, return me to the Muslim cemeteries. From 'A'isha: When the Messenger of Allah died, they differed about his burial. Abu Bakr said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say something I have not forgotten: 'Allah does not take a prophet's soul except in the place where he loves to be buried.' So they buried him in the place of his bed.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
The ruling that burial in houses is makruh is based on two considerations. First, it is a specific privilege (ikhtisas) of the prophets; the Prophet (peace be upon him) was buried in his house as a special honor. Second, the practice of the Sahaba indicates that general burial should be in public cemeteries. The hadith of 'Umar (radi Allahu 'anhu) shows that a person was denied burial in a house and sent to the Muslim cemetery. This establishes that for non-prophets, household burial is disliked (makruh tanzihi). The Hanafi school follows this, allowing it only in exceptional circumstances.

Key Terms
اختصاص (ikhtisas): Specific privilege; something reserved exclusively for a category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a form of shirk
B) It is a specific privilege of prophets
C) It causes hardship to the family
D) The soil is impure

Key Takeaway
Burial in houses is a special privilege for prophets; for the general ummah, it is makruh tanzihi and should be avoided without necessity.

Ruling on Burying in Domed Tombs (Fasaqi)
Ruling on burial in ornate tombs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on burying in fasaqi and explain the two reasons for its dislike.

Core Idea
Burying in fasaqi is makruh tanzihi because it involves building on graves and mixing genders.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on burial in ornate domed structures known as fasaqi. The Hanafi school strongly discourages this practice based on clear prophetic prohibitions and practical concerns. You will learn why even a well-intentioned construction can fall into disliked territory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the act being discussed: burial in fasaqi. Determine the hukm level: makruh tanzihi (disliked).
The ruling is not haram but strongly discouraged.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the prohibition of building on graves (nahy an takhsīṣ al-qubūr). This is based on hadiths such as 'Do not plaster graves, do not build on them.'
The text also mentions a secondary reason: show and pride.
3
Apply the reasons to the ruling
Understand that the first reason (contradicting the prohibition) makes the act makruh. The second reason (gender mingling) adds further weight to the dislike, though the ruling would still be makruh even without it.
Both reasons together strengthen the case for dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره الدفن في الفساقي. (فائدة) الفساقي: هي بناء مزخرف كالقبة يدفن فيه الأغنياء. ويكره لأنها بناء يخالف النهي عن تخصيص القبور، ولأن فيها رياء وتفاخرًا، وكثيرًا ما يدفن فيها الرجال والنساء دون حاجز.

Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This lesson clarifies that burial in 'fasaqi' (large domed mausoleums) is makruh. The author explains that such structures were typically built by wealthy people. The ruling is based on two reasons: first, it contravenes the general prohibition of building elaborate graves (takhsis al-qubur), and second, it often leads to mingling of male and female graves without proper separation, which is inappropriate. The underlying principle is that graves should be simple and without extravagance. The Hanafi school strongly discourages any form of necropolis that resembles royal tombs.

Key Terms
فساقي (fasaqi): Domed or ornate burial structure for the wealthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on Multiple Burials in One Grave
Multiple burials allowed in necessity with soil barrier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple burials in one grave and identify the condition of a soil barrier and the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Multiple burials in one grave are permissible only in necessity, with a soil barrier between each body.

The normal practice is to bury each deceased person in a separate grave. However, Hanafi fiqh recognizes that circumstances of necessity, such as a high number of casualties in war, may require relaxing this rule. This lesson explores the ruling, its condition, and the prophetic evidence that establishes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is burying more than one person in a single grave. The ruling is that it is permissible (la ba'sa) under necessity (darurah).
The default is separate graves; this is a concession.
2
Recognize the condition
A soil barrier (hajz bi al-turab) must be placed between each two bodies to maintain dignity and prevent direct contact.
This condition is explicit in the source text.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Hisham ibn 'Amir from the day of Uhud, recorded in Abu Dawud, provides the evidence.
The Companions asked due to hardship, and the Prophet instructed them accordingly.
4
Analyze the dalil's proof
The Prophet's explicit command to place two or three in one grave indicates permissibility. The command to widen the grave suggests maintaining dignity.
The proof is clear and directly applicable.
5
Note the scope
This is a rukhsa (concession) only when necessity exists. In normal circumstances, separate graves are required.
The ruling is conditional on darurah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بدفن اكثر من واحد في قبر للضرورة ويجحز بين كل اثنين بالتراب. عن هشام بن عامر قال جاءت الانصار الى رسول الله يوم احد فقالوا اصابنا قرح و جهد فكيف تأمرنا ؟ قال احفروا و اوسعوا و اجعلوا الرجلين و الثلاثة في القبر. (ابوداود شریف، باب فی تعمق القبر ،ص ۴۶۹، نمبر ۳۲۱۵).

He said: 'Dig graves, make them wide, and place two or three men in a grave.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
The default rule in Hanafi fiqh is that each person should have their own grave. However, necessity (darurah) permits multiple burials, as demonstrated by the Prophet's instruction at Uhud when many companions were martyred. The condition is that a barrier of soil (hajiz) must be placed between each two bodies to maintain individual dignity. The hadith of Hisham ibn 'Amir provides the primary evidence. The Hanafi school upholds this as a concession (rukhsah).

Key Terms
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that justifies a relaxation of the normal ruling.
حجز (hajz): Barrier; soil placed between bodies to separate them.

Burial at Sea: Conditions and Procedure
Burial at sea when land is far or harm feared

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for burial at sea and identify the two conditions that permit it.

Core Idea
Burial at sea requires full rites and is only allowed when land is distant or harm feared.

What happens when a person dies on a ship far from land? This lesson examines the Hanafi position on burial at sea, which balances funeral dignity with practical necessity. Understanding this ruling prepares you to apply fiqh in challenging circumstances where land burial is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is burial of a deceased person at sea. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) under specific conditions. State the hukm level clearly.
Not obligatory, but a concession.
2
Specify the conditions
The text mentions two conditions: (1) the land is far, or (2) harm (like decay) is feared. Both are alternatives.
These conditions make the permissible act valid.
3
Outline the required procedure
Before sea burial, the body must be washed, shrouded, and the funeral prayer performed. These are the same as land burial rites.
No shortcuts allowed.
4
Examine the evidence
The ruling is based on the statement of Hasan al-Basri, who was a tabi'i. This is a mursal hadith, meaning its chain is incomplete but accepted in practice for fiqh rulings.
Epistemologically zanni al-thubut but clear in meaning.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
While the Hanafi school allows sea burial under these conditions, the Shafi'i school prefers to keep the body on the ship until land if there is no risk of decay.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مات في سفينة وكان البر بعيدا او خيف الضرر غسل وكفن وصلى عليه ويلقى في البحر. عن الحسن البصري انه قال يغسل ويكفن ويصلى عليه ويطرح في البحر. (سنن بیہقی الانسان يموت في البحر، ج رابع ، ص ۱۰، نمبر ۶۷۷۴).

Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This lesson addresses a specific situation: death at sea when immediate burial on land is impossible or when the body would decay. The Hanafi ruling is that the body must be given full honors: ghusl (washing), kafan (shrouding), and salat al-janazah (funeral prayer), and then dropped into the sea. This is based on the statement of Hasan al-Basri (a tabi'i) and is accepted by the Hanafi school. The alternative of keeping the body on the ship for days is not preferred due to risk of decomposition and harm. The ruling ensures respect for the deceased while addressing practical necessity.

Key Terms
ضرر (darar): Harm; here refers to risk of body decay or disease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Definition and Categories of the Shahid in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition of shahid and the killers that qualify one for martyrdom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shahid and identify the four categories of killers that qualify one for martyrdom rulings.

Core Idea
A shahid is anyone killed unjustly by a harbi, rebel, bandit, or night thief — all receive burial without ghusl.

The Hanafi school expands the concept of shahid beyond the battlefield. This lesson presents the four categories of killers whose victims are given the rulings of martyrdom: no ghusl, buried in bloodstained clothes. We will examine the textual evidence for each category and note the difference from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four killer categories
From the text, list the four types: harbi kuffar, ahl al-baghi, bandits (lussus), and a thief entering the house at night.
Note that the thief must be at night and inside the house.
2
State the conditions for shahid rulings
The shahid must not have engaged in worldly benefit after injury (e.g., eaten, drunk, or conducted business). The burial is without ghusl, in his blood and clothes.
These conditions apply to all four categories.
3
Trace the evidence for each category
The text provides: (1) harbi – Quran 2:154 and hadith of Uhud; (2) baghi – saying of Zayd ibn Suhan at the Battle of the Camel; (3) bandits and thief – implied by analogy and the principle of being completely oppressed.
The source cuts off while listing the fourth evidence, but the analogy is clear.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict shahid to battlefield deaths; the Hanafi school extends the rulings to these four categories based on the principle of unjust killing.
The practical difference appears in funeral rites for those killed in civil conflict or by criminals.

Source Text

(970) The shahid is one who is killed by harbi kuffar, or by people of rebellion (baghi), or by bandits, or by a thief in the house at night, even if with a stone.
Explanation: Here, mention is made of four types of killed persons who are like martyrs: they are not given ghusl if they did not benefit from the world after injury; they are buried in their blood and clothes with funeral prayer.[1] First: killed by harbi in the battlefield. [2] Second: killed by rebels (baghi). [3] Third: killed by bandits. [4] Fourth: killed by a thief in the house at night, whether with a sword or a heavy object – all are complete oppressed ones and are buried without ghusl.
Evidence: (1) For those killed by harbi: the verse 'Do not say about those killed in the way of Allah that they are dead; rather they are alive, but you perceive not.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:154). (2) Also hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet ordered for the martyrs of Uhud to remove iron and leather, and to bury them with their blood and clothes. (Abu Dawud) The martyrs of Uhud were killed by harbi. (3) For those killed by rebels (baghi): the saying of Zayd ibn Suhan on the day of Jamal: 'Bury me in the ground, do not wash the blood from me, do not remove my clothes except my khuffs, for I am disputing.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Sunan al-Bayhaqi) Even though both sides were Sahaba, Zayd asked not to be washed, indicating that one killed by baghi is not given ghusl. (4) This saying of the Companion...
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This lesson defines the shahid according to the Hanafi school: a person killed by one of four types of aggressors – harbi kuffar (in war), rebels (baghi), bandits (lussus), or a thief entering the house at night – regardless of the weapon used. The key conditions for the martyrdom rulings (no ghusl, buried in bloodstained clothes) are that the person did not engage in worldly benefit after injury and was unjustly killed. The evidence is sequential: for harbi, Quran and hadith; for baghi, a saying of the companion Zayd ibn Suhan from the Battle of the Camel, which shows that even inter-Muslim conflict can produce martyrs. The text also implies that the same rulings apply to those killed by bandits and thieves based on analogy (qiyas) and the principle of being completely oppressed (mazlum kamil).

Key Terms
شهيد (shahid): One killed unjustly by harbi, baghi, bandit, or night thief, qualifying for martyrdom rulings
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims
أهل البغي (ahl al-baghi): Rebel group that fights against the legitimate Muslim ruler
لص (liss): Thief or bandit, especially one who enters a house at night

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Washing the Martyr: Conditions of Irtithāth and Janābah
Ruling on washing the martyr with proofs from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing a martyr, distinguish between the conditions of irtithāth and janābah, and apply the evidence from the hadith of Hanzalah.

Core Idea
A martyr not washed if no worldly benefit and no janābah; but if junub, washing for impurity remains wajib.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on washing the martyr (shahīd). The key condition is irtithāth—whether the wounded person benefited from worldly life after the injury. Additionally, a martyr in a state of janābah must be washed for that impurity, as proven by the incident of Hanzalah. Understanding these rulings is essential for properly handling the funeral rites of martyrs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its base ruling
The act is washing the deceased Muslim. For a martyr (shahīd), the general ruling is that washing is waived if certain conditions are met.
The martyr is honored by not being washed, as his blood is considered a testimony.
2
Determine the condition of irtithāth
Irtithāth means benefiting from worldly life after being wounded (e.g., eating, drinking, using medicine). If the martyr did not benefit, he is not washed. If he did benefit, he is washed like an ordinary deceased.
The condition is checked after the end of the war.
3
Identify the exception for janābah
Even if the martyr did not benefit (so washing for death is waived), if he was in a state of janābah (major impurity) at the time of death, he must be washed for that impurity.
This also applies to menstruation and postpartum bleeding.
4
Examine the dalil for janābah exception
The hadith of Hanzalah (رضي الله عنه) narrates that the angels washed him because he was junub when martyred. This proves that janābah requires washing regardless of martyrdom.
The proof is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Mustadrak al-Hakim.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab perspective
The Hanafi position is that a junub martyr is washed. Other schools may differ, and this difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical consequence is whether funeral prayer can be performed without washing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
14.
باب احكام الشهيد
(۹۷۳) ولم يرتت بعد انقضاء الحرب
تشریح : کافر پر نماز ہی کا سوال نہیں ہے اس لئے مسلمان ہو پس اگر بالغ ہے تو ایسا نا پاک نہ ہو جس سے غسل واجب ہو تو غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا، مثلا اگر شہید جنبی ہو یا حیض یا نفاس کی حالت میں مرا ہو تو حنفیہ کے نزدیک اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا۔ متن میں بالغ کی قید لگائی، کیونکہ اگر بچہ شہید ہوا ہو تو اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا۔
وجه: (ا)۔حدیث میں ہے حدثنی یحیی بن عباد بن عبدالله ... حنظلة بن ابی عامر قال فقال رسول الله ان صاحبكم تغسله الملائكة فاسئلوا صاحبته فقالت خرج وهو جنب لما سمع الهائعة فقال رسول الله لذلك غسلته الملائكة (سن لليهقي ، باب الحب يستشهد في المعركة ج رابع ص ۲ نمبر ۶۸۱۴، کتاب الجنائز مستدرک حاکم ، ذکر مناقب خظلة بن عبد الله ، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۲۵، نمبر ۴۹۱۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت حنظلہ جنبی تھے اور فرشتوں نے ان کو غسل دیا اسلئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک جنبی شہید کو نسل دیا جائے گا۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں دو نسل واجب ہونے کا تذکرہ ہے . عن الحسن قال : اذا مات الجنب قال : يغسل غسلا لجنابته و يغسل غسل الميت و کذالک قوله فی
الحائض اذا طهرت ثم ماتت قبل أن تغسل . (مصنف ابن ابی هیبت ، باب ۳۲، فی الجنب والحائض يموتان ما يصنع بهما، ج ثانی ،ص ۴۵۹، نمبر ۱۱۰۱۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جنبی اور حائضہ اور نفساء پر دو نسل ہیں، ایک جنابت کی وجہ سے اور دوسری موت کی وجہ سے۔ اس لئے شہادت کی وجہ سے موت غسل ساقط ہو گیا ہے، لیکن جنابت کا غسل واجب ہوگا۔
ترجمه : (۹۷۳) اور جنگ کے ختم ہونے کے بعد زیادہ فائدہ نہ اٹھایا ہو۔ تشریح : ارتثاث کا معنی ہے فائدہ اٹھانا، زخم لگنے کے بعد شہید ہونے والا آدمی ہوش کی حالت میں کھانا نہ کھایا ہو، دو و غیرہ نہ کی ہوتو وہ کامل مظلوم ہے اس کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا لیکن اگر زخم لگنے اور جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھایا ہو تو وہ شہدا ءاحد کی
طرح کامل مظلوم نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو غسل دیا جائے گا۔۔ ارتثاث : رث سے مشتق ہے، زخمی کو میدان جنگ سے لانا۔ وجه : (۱) اس کی دلیل یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عمر بن ميمون في قصة قتل عمر حين طعنه قال فطار العلج
بالسكين ذات طرفين لا يمر على احد يمينا ولا شمالا الا طعنه وفى ذلك دلالة على انه قتل بمحدد ثم غسل و كفن وصلى عليه (سنن سیتی ، باب الرحث الخ، ج رابع ص ۲۵ نمبر ۶۸۲) اس اثر میں حضرت عمر کو زخم لگنے کے بعد انہوں نے کھایا پیا ہے، اس لئے ان کو غسل دیا گیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زخم لگنے کے بعد جس نے دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھایا اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا۔ (۲) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا رفع القتيل دفن في ثيابه و ان رفع به رمق صنع به ما صنع بغيره ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۲۹، فی الرجل يقتل أو يستشهد يدفن كما هو او يغسل ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۰۰۳)(۳). عن الحسن و حماد و الحكم عن ابراهيم قال : اذا مات في المعركة دفن و نزع ما كان عليه من خف أو نعل ، و اذا رفع
(973) And he did not benefit after the end of the war. Commentary: The disbeliever is not even questioned about prayer, so if he is a Muslim and an adult, and he is not in a state that makes ghusl obligatory, then ghusl will not be given. For example, if the martyr is junub or died in a state of menstruation or postpartum bleeding, according to the Hanafis, he will be given ghusl. The text specifies 'adult' because if a child is martyred, he will be given ghusl. Evidence: (1) In a hadith: Yahya ibn Abbad narrated... Hanzalah ibn Abi Amir said: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Your companion is being washed by the angels, so ask his wife.' She said, 'He left while he was junub when he heard the battle cry.' The Messenger of Allah said, 'That is why the angels washed him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This indicates that Hanzalah was junub and the angels washed him, so according to the Hanafis, a junub martyr should be washed. (2) The saying of a tabi'i mentions two obligatory washes: from Hasan: when a junub dies, he should be washed once for his janabah and once for burial. Similarly for menstruating woman if she becomes purified and dies before washing. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This indicates that for a junub, menstruating, or postpartum woman, two washes are required: one for impurity and one for death. So the wash due to martyrdom is dropped, but the wash for janabah remains obligatory. Translation: (973) And he did not greatly benefit after the end of the war. Commentary: Irtithath means benefiting. If a person who is about to be martyred after being wounded did not eat in a conscious state or drink, he is completely wronged and will not be washed. But if he benefited from the world after being wounded and the war ended, he is not like the martyrs of Uhud in being completely wronged, so he will be washed. Irtithath is derived from rath, meaning bringing the wounded from the battlefield. Evidence: (1) This proof is the saying of a companion: from Umar ibn Maymun regarding the story of Umar's murder when he was stabbed: he flew with a double-edged knife... then he was washed, shrouded, and prayed upon. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This indicates that after being wounded, Umar ate and drank, so he was washed, showing that if one benefits from the world after being wounded, he is washed. (2) From Ibrahim: when the slain is carried, he is buried in his clothes, and if he has any life remaining, he is treated like others. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) (3) From al-Hasan, Hammad, and al-Hakam from Ibrahim: when one dies in battle, he is buried and his khuff or sandal is removed, and if he is carried...
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs concerning the washing of the martyr (shahīd). It begins by stating the condition of irtithāth (benefiting from worldly life after the wound). If the martyr did not benefit (i.e., did not eat, drink, or use medicine) after being wounded and before the war ended, he is considered a complete martyr (kāmil mazlūm) and is not washed. However, if he did benefit, he is treated like an ordinary deceased person and must be washed. The author then addresses a secondary issue: if the martyr is in a state of janābah (major ritual impurity), menstruation, or postpartum bleeding, the Hanafis rule that he must be washed for that impurity, even though the martyr's wash for death is waived. The proof for this is the hadith of Hanzalah, who was junub and was washed by angels, indicating that janābah requires washing. Additionally, the athar from Hasan al-Basri states that a junub person needs two washes: one for janābah and one for death, but since martyrdom removes the death wash, only the janābah wash remains. The author also cites the incident of 'Umar ibn al-Khattāb who, after being stabbed, ate and drank, thus benefiting, so he was washed. This supports the rule that benefiting nullifies the martyr's exemption from washing.

Key Terms
ارتثاث (irtithāth): Benefiting from worldly life after being wounded, such as eating, drinking, or using medicine, before death.
شهید (shahīd): One who is killed in battle against disbelievers, with certain conditions; may be washed or not depending on state.
جنابت (janābah): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, typically from sexual intercourse or discharge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following martyrs must be washed?
A) A martyr who was in a state of janābah.
B) A martyr who did not benefit after the wound and was not junub.
C) All martyrs are washed.
D) A martyr who was killed instantly without any worldly benefit.

Key Takeaway
A martyr is washed only if he benefited after the wound (irtithāth) or was in a state of major impurity (janābah, hayd, nifas); otherwise, washing is waived.

The Martyr's Shroud and Funeral Prayer Without Washing
Ruling with proof from Sunnah and practice of Uhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the martyr's shroud and prayer, identify the conditions that make a martyr eligible for this treatment, and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The martyr is not washed but shrouded in his bloodstained clothes and the funeral prayer is offered over him.

Ensuring proper burial rites for martyrs is a matter of great significance. The Hanafi school has a distinct position based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ at the Battle of Uhud. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence that supports it, clarifying a common area of confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
What exactly is the ruling for the martyr regarding washing, shrouding, and prayer? Extract the three elements.
The matn states: shrouded in his blood and clothes, prayed upon without washing.
2
List the Conditions
The commentary mentions conditions that must be met for this ruling to apply. Identify them.
Conditions: killed oppressively, not in a state of janabah, did not benefit from the world after the wound.
3
Examine the Primary Evidence
The first hadith cited is from Jabir about the command 'Bury them in their blood.' Understand how this proves the ruling.
The Prophet's command and action at Uhud is the core proof.
4
Confirm the Funeral Prayer
The author provides multiple hadiths showing that the Prophet prayed over the martyrs of Uhud. Trace this proof.
The prayer is confirmed by the actions of the Prophet.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some scholars hold that the martyr should be washed. Understand the Hanafi response to this.
Hanafis adhere to the literal practice; this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢
۱۶۱
باب احكام الشهيد
(۹۷۴) فيـكـفـن بــدمـه وثيابه و يصلى عليه بلا غسل (۹۷۵) وينزع عنه ما ليس صالحا للكفن
ترجمه : (۹۷۴) کفن دیا جائے گا اسی خون اور اس کپڑے میں اور اس پر بغیر نسل کے نماز پڑھی جائے گی [ اور دفن کر دیا جائے گا تشریح : حاصل یہ ہے کہ ظلم کامل کے ساتھ قتل کیا گیا ہو، اور جنبی وغیرہ نہ ہو، اور زخم لگنے کے بعد دنیا سے فائدہ نہ اٹھایا ہو تو وہ دنیا کے اعتبار سے شہید ہے اس کو اسی کپڑے اور خون میں لپیٹا جائے گا اور بغیر غسل دئے اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور دفن کر دیا جائے گا شہداءاحد کے ساتھ ایسا ہی کیا گیا تھا۔ وجه : (۱) کفن دیا جائے گا اور غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عـن جـابـر قـال النبي له ادفنوهم في دمائهم يعني يوم احد ولم يغسلهم ( بخاری شریف ، باب من لم ير غسل الشہید ص ۱۷۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۶ ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الشہید یغسل ج ثانی ص ۹۱ نمبر ۳۱۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہید کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا، اور اسی خون میں دفن کیا جائے گا۔ (۲) اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال اتى بهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم احد
للبيهقي
صلى الله
فجعل يصلى على عشرة عشرة و حمزة هو كما هو يرفعون وهو كما هو موضوع. (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء في الصلوة على الشهداء وفتحهم ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۱۵/۱۳/رسن له ، باب من زعم ان النبی اللہ صلی علی شہداء احد، ج رابع ص ۱۸ نمبر ۶۸۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہداء احد پر آپ نے نماز پڑھی (۳) نماز ترقی درجات کے لئے اور استغفار کے لئے ہے۔ اور یہ بچوں اور نبی کے لئے بھی جائز ہے۔ اس لئے شہید کے لئے بھی کیا جائے (۴) خود بخاری میں اس حدیث میں موجود
صلى الله
صلہ
ہے۔ عن عقبة بن عامر ان النبي عل خرج يوما فصلى على اهل احد صلواته على الميت ثم انصرف الى لــــمــــبـــــر ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی الشہید ص ۷۹ نمبر ۱۳۴۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہید پر نماز پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلوة على الشهيد وغسله ج ثالث ص ۶۵۳ نمبر ۶۶۶۶/۶۶۶۷ میں شہید پر نماز پڑھنے کے بارے میں تفصیل موجود ہے. فليراجع ! (۵) عن عقبة بن عامر الجهني : أن النبي الله صلى على قتلى أحد صلاته على الميت . (مستدرک حاکم، کتاب الجنائز، ج، اول، ص ۵۲۰، نمبر ۱۳۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ میت پر جس طرح نماز پڑھتے ہیں اسی طرح شہداء احد پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی۔
(974) He will be shrouded in his blood and his clothes, and prayer will be performed over him without washing. (975) And what is not suitable for the shroud is removed from him. Translation: (974) He will be shrouded in that same blood and that cloth, and prayer will be performed over him without washing, and he will be buried. Commentary: The summary is that if he was killed with complete oppression, and he was not junub etc., and he did not benefit from the world after being wounded, then he is a martyr in worldly terms. He will be wrapped in his clothes and blood, without washing, prayer will be performed over him, and he will be buried. This was done with the martyrs of Uhud. Evidence: (1) The shroud is given but not washed. The proof is the hadith from Jabir: The Prophet said, 'Bury them in their blood' meaning on the day of Uhud, and he did not wash them. (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) (2) Prayer over him is performed. The proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah came to them on the day of Uhud and began to pray over ten by ten, and Hamzah was as he was, they were lifted and he was as he was placed. (Ibn Majah, al-Bayhaqi) (3) Prayer is for elevation of ranks and seeking forgiveness, and it is permissible for children and prophets, so it is also done for the martyr. (4) In Bukhari, from Uqbah ibn Amir: The Prophet went out one day and prayed over the people of Uhud his prayer over the deceased, then went to the pulpit. (Bukhari) (5) From Uqbah ibn Amir al-Juhani: The Prophet prayed over the slain of Uhud his prayer over the deceased. (Mustadrak al-Hakim)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proofs for how a martyr is to be buried. The martyr who meets the conditions (killed oppressively, not junub, without benefiting after the wound) is not washed. Instead, he is shrouded in the clothes he was wearing, stained with his blood, and buried without removing any bloodstains. The funeral prayer is offered over him. The main proof is from the Battle of Uhud, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that the martyrs be buried in their blood without washing, and he himself performed the funeral prayer over them in groups. The author also provides rational arguments: prayer is for seeking forgiveness and elevating ranks, which is also beneficial for the martyr. The sources cited include Sahih al-Bukhari, Sunan Abi Dawud, Sunan Ibn Majah, and al-Mustadrak.

Key Terms
کفن (kafan): Shroud: the cloth in which the deceased is wrapped. For the martyr, his own clothes serve as the shroud.
شهيد (shahīd): Martyr: one who is killed unjustly in battle and meets the conditions to be considered a shahīd al-dunyā (worldly martyr) with special burial rites.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the deceased; for the martyr, this is omitted.
جنبي (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl before prayer. If a martyr is junub, he must be washed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true about the martyr who dies in battle without benefiting after the wound?
A) He is washed, shrouded, and prayed upon.
B) He is not washed, not shrouded, and not prayed upon.
C) He is not washed, but is shrouded in his blood-stained clothes and prayed upon.
D) He is washed but not shrouded.

Key Takeaway
The martyr who meets the conditions (killed oppressively, not junub, no worldly benefit after wound) is not washed but is shrouded in his bloodstained clothes and the funeral prayer is offered over him.

Removing Items Unsuitable for Shroud from the Martyr
Ruling on removing unsuitable items from the martyr's shroud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which items are removed from the martyr's shroud and explain the basis for the adjustment to the sunnah length.

Core Idea
A martyr's shroud is his clothes, but items like weapons and armor are removed as they are unsuitable for shrouding.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the burial of a martyr. While the martyr is buried in the clothes he wore at the time of death, not everything he was wearing remains. Items that are not appropriate for use as a shroud are removed, and the cloth is adjusted to conform to the sunnah length. The passage provides specific examples to clarify the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that the act in question is removing certain items from the martyr's body before burial. The ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) to remove items that are not suitable for the shroud.
The ruling is based on the practice of the Companions.
2
List the Examples Given
From the text, list the items that are to be removed: fur coats (paustin), rags (gudri), weapons (hathiyar), and armor (zarah). These are not considered proper shrouding material.
The examples help define 'unsuitable' for shrouding.
3
Explain the Adjustment to Sunnah Length
After removing unsuitable items, the remaining cloth (the martyr's clothes) is adjusted—either reduced or increased—so that it meets the sunnah length for a shroud. This ensures the body is properly covered according to the prophetic practice.
This shows flexibility to fulfill the sunnah while using the martyr's own clothes.
4
Note the Underlying Principle
The underlying principle is that the martyr's burial should honor his status while adhering to the sunnah. His clothes serve as the shroud, but only what is fitting for burial remains.
The martyr is not treated entirely like an ordinary deceased; his blood and clothes are blessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۹۷۵) وينزع عنه ما ليس صالحا للكفن
ترجمه : (۹۷۵) اور اس سے نکالی جائے گی وہ چیز جو کفن کے قابل نہ ہو، مثلا پوستین اور گودڑی اور ہتھیار اور زرہ۔ اور اس کپڑے میں سنت کفن کے موافق کم و بیش کر دیا جائے۔
(975) And what is not suitable for the shroud is removed from him. Translation: And from him will be removed that which is not suitable for the shroud, for example, fur, rags, weapons, and armor. And in that cloth, it should be reduced or increased according to the sunnah of the shroud.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that items that are not appropriate for use as a shroud are to be removed from the martyr before burial. Examples include animal skins (fur coats, leather), tattered rags, and weapons or armor. The shroud should consist of the clothes the martyr was wearing, but if they are insufficient according to the sunnah, more cloth may be added. Conversely, if the clothes are more than the sunnah requires, they may be reduced. The practice is to dress the martyr in a proper shroud, considering the sunnah of covering the body adequately.

Key Terms
کفن (kafan): Shroud: the cloth covering the deceased. For the martyr, his own clothes constitute the shroud, but unsuitable items are removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is removed from the martyr before burial?
A) His turban
B) His leather armor (zarah)
C) His shirt
D) His trousers

Key Takeaway
Items unsuitable for shrouding, such as weapons and armor, are removed from the martyr, and the cloth is adjusted to the sunnah length.

The Three Rulings for the Shahid: Shroud, Washing, and Prayer
Definition and three primary rulings with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three funeral rulings for a shahid, identify the conditions that define a shahid, and explain the proof from the Sunnah for each ruling.

Core Idea
A martyr is shrouded in his blood and buried unwashed; the funeral prayer is performed over him — based on the Prophetic practice at Uhud.

The term 'shahid' carries both worldly and hereafter meanings. In the context of funeral rulings, the Hanafi school defines a shahid as someone killed unjustly in battle who did not benefit from worldly life after the wound. This passage lays out three distinct rulings that apply to such a person: the way he is shrouded, the prohibition of washing, and the obligation of prayer. These rulings are derived directly from the actions of the Prophet ﷺ regarding the martyrs of Uhud. Let us examine the conditions and the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and conditions of a shahid
The passage defines a shahid for worldly rulings as one killed unjustly in battle, not in a state of janabah, and who did not survive long enough to benefit from worldly life after the wound. Note that if any condition is missing (e.g., he had a ramaq and was treated), the ruling changes.
The term 'ramaq' is key: if he had a spark of life and was taken alive, he is treated as a normal deceased person.
2
State the three rulings explicitly
From the passage: (1) He is shrouded in his blood and the clothes he was wearing. (2) He is not given ghusl (ritual washing). (3) The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is performed over him. Each ruling has a distinct legal classification.
The shroud is wajib, the prohibition of washing is makruh tahrimi or haram, and the prayer is fard kifayah.
3
Connect each ruling to its proof from the Sunnah
The passage cites multiple hadith. For the shroud and no washing: the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet ordered 'Bury them in their blood' and did not wash them. For the prayer: hadith of Ibn Abbas and Uqba ibn Amir showing the Prophet prayed over the Uhud martyrs.
The proofs are ahad hadith, and their thubut and dalala are zanni, but they are sufficient for Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the rationale behind the prayer
The passage explains that the funeral prayer is for raising ranks and seeking forgiveness. It is performed for martyrs just as it is for children and the Prophet himself, indicating that it is not only permissible but recommended.
This refutes the view of some other schools that martyrs are not prayed over.
5
Compare with other madhahib (optional for advanced)
While Hanafis hold that prayer is performed, some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) differ on certain points. However, the Hanafi position is based on clear Prophetic practice and has been relied upon in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
The key difference is whether the prayer is performed; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Chapter on the rulings of the martyr. (974) He is shrouded in his blood and clothes, and prayer is performed over him without washing. (975) And what is not suitable for the shroud is removed from him. If he had a spark of life and then died, he is treated like a dead person. Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, section 29, regarding a man killed or martyred, buried as he is and washed... In both these athars: if he was taken alive from the battlefield and benefited [from worldly life], then he will be washed like other dead. Translation: (974) He will be shrouded in that blood and that cloth, and the funeral prayer will be performed over him without washing, and he will be buried. Explanation: The summary is that if he was killed with complete injustice, and was not in a state of janabah etc., and did not benefit from worldly life after being wounded, then he is a martyr from a worldly perspective; he will be wrapped in his cloth and blood, and the prayer will be performed over him without washing, and he will be buried. This is what was done with the martyrs of Uhud. Evidence: (1) He will be shrouded and not washed: the proof is the hadith of Jabir: The Prophet ﷺ said, 'Bury them in their blood' on the day of Uhud, and he did not wash them. (Bukhari, Baihaqi) This hadith shows that the martyr is not washed and is buried in his blood. (2) Prayer will be performed over him: the proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ came on the day of Uhud and began to pray over ten by ten, while Hamza was as he was, they were lifted and he was as he was placed. (Ibn Majah, Baihaqi) This hadith shows that the Prophet prayed over the martyrs of Uhud. (3) Prayer is for raising ranks and seeking forgiveness, and it is permissible for children and the Prophet, so it is done for the martyr. (4) In Bukhari itself there is the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir: The Prophet ﷺ went out one day and prayed over the martyrs of Uhud like his prayer over the dead, then he returned to the pulpit. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that prayer can be performed over the martyr. (5) From Uqba ibn Amir al-Juhani: The Prophet ﷺ prayed over the slain of Uhud like his prayer over the dead. (Mustadrak Hakim) This hadith states that the Prophet prayed the funeral prayer over the martyrs of Uhud just as one prays over the dead.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the chapter on the martyr. It first defines the shahid (martyr) in the worldly sense as someone killed unjustly in battle, not in a state of janabah, and who did not survive long enough to benefit from worldly life after the wound. The three main rulings are: (i) he is shrouded in his blood and the clothes he was wearing at the time of death—this is a wajib act; (ii) he is not washed—this is a prohibition (haram or makruh tahrimi) to wash him; (iii) the funeral prayer is performed over him—this is fard kifayah. The text then provides evidence from authentic hadith for each ruling. For the prohibition of washing, it cites the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet ordered the martyrs of Uhud to be buried in their blood without washing. For the prayer, it cites multiple hadith showing that the Prophet himself prayed over the martyrs of Uhud, either in batches or individually. The text also explains that the prayer is for intercession and forgiveness, and since it is done for children and prophets, it is also done for martyrs. The student should note that the conditions for these rulings are precisely: the killing must be unjust, the martyr must not be in major impurity, and he must not have had any worldly benefit after the injury. If any of these conditions is absent, the ruling changes (e.g., if he had a 'spark of life' and was treated, he is washed normally).

Key Terms
شهيد (shahid): Here: a person killed unjustly in battle, not in janabah, and who did not benefit from worldly life after the wound; considered a martyr for worldly rulings.
رمق (ramaq): The remaining spark of life; if the person had a ramaq (i.e., was taken alive and benefited from worldly things), he is not treated as a martyr.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the deceased; prohibited for the martyr under the conditions stated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He is not washed, shrouded in his blood and clothes, and prayed upon
C) He is washed, not shrouded, and not prayed upon

Key Takeaway
A shahid (worldly martyr) is shrouded in his blood, not washed, and the funeral prayer is performed over him based on the Sunnah of the Prophet at Uhud.

Preparing the Martyr's Shroud
Ruling with proof on martyr's shroud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for preparing a martyr's shroud: what must be removed, what is added, and what is disliked, and identify the supporting evidence.

Core Idea
A martyr is buried in his own clothes — unsuitable items removed, but stripping him completely is disliked.

This passage specifies how a martyr's burial shroud is handled. It distinguishes between items that must be removed because they are not suitable for shrouding (like weapons and armor) and those that are kept. It also addresses when the shroud is deficient and what is disliked. The evidence comes from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that this ruling applies specifically to a martyr (shahid) who died in battle. The shroud is his own clothing that he was wearing at the time of death.
This is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different rules.
2
List what must be removed
From the martyr's body, remove items not suitable for a shroud: leather garments (firw), padded coats (hashw), weapons (silah), and armor (dir'). This is wajib.
These items are considered impure or inappropriate for burial.
3
Determine the ruling on adding or decreasing cloth
If the martyr’s clothes are insufficient to cover the body according to sunnah (head to toe), add extra cloth to complete the shroud. If more than needed, it is not wasted but kept.
The example of Mus‘ab ibn ‘Umayr shows addition is allowed.
4
Recognize the disliked action
Removing all of the martyr’s clothes, even those suitable for shrouding, is makruh tanzihi. He will be resurrected in those bloodstained clothes as evidence of his martyrdom.
The statement of Zayd ibn Suhan confirms this.
5
Examine the evidence
The proofs are: (a) hadith of Ibn Abbas – Prophet ordered iron and leather removed from martyrs of Uhud; (b) hadith of Khabbab – insufficient shroud was supplemented; (c) saying of Zayd – do not remove clothes except khuffayn.
All are ahad hadith but accepted in practice.

(مسلم شریف ، باب فی کفن میت ،ص ۳۷۹، نمبر ۲۱۷۷٫۹۴۰ را بود او د شریف، باب کراھیة المغالاة في الكفن ص ۴۶۱ نمبر ۳۱۵۵) اس حدیث میں کفن کم تھا بلکہ تھاہی نہیں تو چادر کفن کے لئے دی گئی۔ لغت : میزع: نزع سے مشتق ہے، نکال لیا جائے، کھینچ لیا جائے ۔ الفرو : چمڑے کالباس، الحشو : ایسالباس جس میں روئی بھری ہو، کوٹ وغیرہ، السلاح : ہتھیار - Translation: (975) And from him will be removed what is not suitable for the shroud, such as fur coat and patched garment and weapons and armor. And in his clothes, he is increased or decreased according to the sunnah of the shroud. Like the fur, padding, weapons, and armor, and it is increased and decreased in his clothes. (976) And it is disliked to remove all of them. (977) And he is washed if a child, insane, menstruating, postpartum, or junub is killed. Explanation: From the body of the martyr, what is not suitable for the shroud will be removed, and if the sunnah shroud is deficient, it will be increased so that the shroud conforms to the sunnah. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ commanded regarding the slain of Uhud that the iron and leather be removed from them, and that they be buried in their blood and clothes. (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah) This hadith shows that clothes that are not suitable for the shroud are removed, and those that are suitable remain. (2) If the shroud is insufficient, it is increased: the hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: We emigrated with the Messenger of Allah... Mus'ab ibn Umayr was killed on the day of Uhud, and nothing was found to shroud him except a striped garment. When we placed it over his head, his feet came out; when we placed it over his feet, his head came out. So the Messenger of Allah said: 'Place it over his head and put idhkhir over his feet.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) In this hadith, the shroud was insufficient, so a sheet was given for the shroud. Lexicon: yunza': derived from naza'a, removed; al-firw: leather garment; al-hashw: garment filled with cotton, like a coat; al-silah: weapons; al-dir': armor. Translation: (976) Yes, it is disliked to remove all his clothes. Explanation: It is disliked to remove those clothes that are suitable for the shroud from the martyr, because he will appear on the Day of Resurrection with those bloodstained clothes and will argue (with blood as evidence). Evidence: (1) Zayd ibn Suhan said on the Day of Jamal: 'Bury me in the ground without washing any blood from me, and do not remove any garment from me except the khuffayn, for I will argue (with my blood).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof covering two sub-rulings. First (975): From the martyr, items that are not suitable for a shroud are removed. These include leather garments (firw), padded coats (hashw), weapons (silah), and armor (dir'). The clothes that are suitable are kept, but if they are insufficient to cover the body according to the sunnah (i.e., the normal amount of shroud cloth), additional cloth is added to make the shroud complete. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ordered iron and leather to be removed from the martyrs of Uhud. Another hadith of Khabbab illustrates that when a shroud is insufficient, extra material is added. Second (976): It is makruh (disliked) to remove all of the martyr's clothes, even those that are not suitable? Actually the text says it is disliked to remove all of them (i.e., all the clothes, including those suitable for shrouding). The reason is that the martyr will rise on the Day of Resurrection with his bloodstained clothes, and he will argue (to testify) with that blood. The evidence is the statement of Zayd ibn Suhan. The student should note the distinction: items that are not suitable for shrouding (like weapons and armor) must be removed; but clothes that are suitable should not be removed entirely. The ruling of karahah (dislike) applies to removing all clothes, especially those that can serve as a shroud.

Key Terms
كفن (kafan): The shroud used to wrap the deceased. For the martyr, it is his own clothes after removing unsuitable items.
نزع (naza'a): Removing items from the martyr's body; specifically items not suitable for burial.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; here it refers to the act of removing all the martyr's clothes, which is makruh tanzihi.
فرو (firw): Leather garment; considered not suitable for shrouding.
حشو (hashw): Padded garment, e.g., a coat filled with cotton; not suitable as shroud.
سلاح (silah): Weapons; must be removed.
درع (dir'): Armor; must be removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following items should be removed from the martyr before burial?
A) His ordinary clothes suitable for shrouding
B) Leather garments and weapons
C) All of his clothes
D) Only his headgear

Key Takeaway
The martyr is buried in his own clothes after removing items unsuitable for shrouding; removing all clothes is makruh.

The Martyr's Shroud: Removal and Completion
Ruling with proof on martyr's shroud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on removing non-shroud items and completing the deficient shroud of a battlefield martyr, and explain why removing all clothes is makruh.

Core Idea
The martyr is buried in his own clothes; remove non-shroud items and supplement if insufficient, but never strip him bare.

This lesson examines the specific rulings for shrouding a battlefield martyr (shahid) according to the Hanafi school. While a regular deceased person is washed and wrapped in a new shroud, the martyr is buried in his own clothes after removing items that are not part of the sunnah shroud, such as weapons and armor. If the clothes are insufficient to cover the body, additional cloth is added. The passage also explains that removing all the martyr’s clothes is disliked (makruh) because he will rise on the Day of Judgment with his blood-stained clothes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is shrouding the martyr (kafan al-shahid). It is an obligation (wajib) that follows specific rules distinct from ordinary shrouding.
The martyr is not washed; his own clothes serve as shroud.
2
Locate the proofs
The author cites two hadith: (1) Ibn Abbas reports the Prophet ordered removal of iron and skins from Uhud martyrs and burial with their blood and clothes. (2) Khabbab narrates the incident of Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr where the Prophet instructed to place a cloak on his head and cover his feet with grass due to shroud deficiency.
Also, Zayd ibn Suhan's statement supports not removing all clothes.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the first hadith, the command 'an yunza' indicates removal of non-shroud items, and 'yudfanu bi dima'ihim wa thiyabihim' shows clothes remain. From the second hadith, the Prophet's action of adding cloth shows supplementation of deficient shroud.
The word 'izad' (increase) in the matn is derived from this hadith.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki) wash and shroud the martyr normally; Hanafi distinguishes because the martyr's blood testifies. The Hanafi position is based on the explicit command of the Prophet.
The martyr's clothes are left bloody as a witness.
5
Note the ruling on removing all clothes
The matn states it is makruh to remove all clothes. The commentary explains that the martyr will appear on the Day of Judgment with his blood-stained clothes and will argue (yuḥājj). The proof is from Zayd ibn Suhan who said he wants to argue with his clothes.
This ruling applies to clothes suitable for shrouding; non-shroud items must be removed.

وجه : (۱)قال زيد بن صوحان يوم الجمل: ارمسونى فى الارض رمسا و لا تغسلوا عنى دما و لا تنزعوا عنى ثوبا الا الخفين فانی محاج احاج . مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ،۲۹، في الرجل يقتل أو يستشهد يدفن كما هو و يغسل ، ج ثانی ص ۷ ۴۵ ، نمبر ۱۰۹۹۷ رسن بیہقی ، باب ماورد فی المقتول بسیف اهل البغی ، ج رابع ، ص ۲۶، نمبر ۶۸۲۴)
Chapter: Rulings on the Martyr. Like fur, padding, weapons, and armor; and it is increased and decreased in his clothes (976). And it is disliked to remove all of them (977). Commentary: From the body of the martyr, items that are not suitable for the shroud will be removed; and if the shroud is deficient according to the sunnah, then it will be increased so that the shroud conforms to the sunnah. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, ordered concerning the slain of Uhud that the iron and skins be removed from them, and that they be buried with their blood and clothes.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Shahid Yughsal, p. 459, no. 3134; Ibn Majah, Bab ma Ja'a fi al-Salat 'ala al-Shuhada', p. 216, no. 1515). This hadith indicates that clothes or items not suitable for the shroud should be removed, and clothes suitable for the shroud should be kept with them. (2) If the shroud is deficient, it is increased. For this, there is this hadith: From Khabbab ibn al-Aratt: 'We migrated with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, seeking the face of Allah. Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr was killed on the day of Uhud. Nothing was found to shroud him except a cloak. When we placed it over his head, his feet came out; when we placed it over his feet, his head came out. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Place it on his head and put idhkhir on his feet.' (Muslim, Bab fi Kafan al-Mayyit, p. 379, no. 2177/940; Abu Dawud, Bab Karahiyat al-Mughalat fi al-Kafan, p. 461, no. 3155). In this hadith, the shroud was deficient, rather it was non-existent, so a sheet was given for the shroud. Lexicon: 'Miz'a': derived from 'naza', to remove, to pull out; 'al-farw': leather garment; 'al-hashw': garment filled with cotton, coat, etc.; 'al-silah': weapons; 'al-dir': armor. Translation: (976) Yes, removing all his clothes is disliked. Commentary: Removing clothes suitable for the shroud from the martyr is disliked, because he will appear on the Day of Judgment with those blood-stained clothes and will argue. Evidence: (1) Zayd ibn Suhan said on the day of Jamal: 'Bury me in the earth, do not wash the blood from me, and do not remove any garment from me except the khuffayn, for I am arguing.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab 29, fi al-Rajul Yuqtal aw Yustashhad Yudfan Kama Huwa wa Yughsal, vol. 2, p. 45, no. 10997; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma Warada fi al-Maqtul bi-Sayf Ahl al-Baghy, vol. 4, p. 26, no. 6824)
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) concerning the shroud (kafan) of the martyr (shahid). The matn states that items like fur, padded garments, weapons, and armor – which are not part of the sunnah shroud – must be removed. However, if the martyr's clothing is insufficient for a proper shroud according to sunnah, additional cloth is added to cover the body. It is also disliked (makruh) to remove all the clothes from the martyr; rather, the clothes that are suitable for the shroud should be left on, as the martyr will rise with them on the Day of Judgment. The commentary supports these rulings with two hadith: one from Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet ﷺ ordered the removal of iron and skins from the martyrs of Uhud, and another from Khabbab about Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr where the Prophet ﷺ instructed to place the cloak on the head and cover the feet with Idhkhir (a fragrant grass), demonstrating how to handle a deficient shroud. The prohibition of removing all clothes is supported by the tradition of Zayd ibn Suhan, who asked to be buried with his clothes except the khuff (leather socks) because he would argue (i.e., present his martyrdom). The Hanafi position is clear: the martyr is buried in his own clothes after removing non-kafan items; if the clothes are insufficient, the shroud is completed from other cloth; and it is makruh to remove all clothes.

Key Terms
الشهيد (al-shahīd): The martyr who is killed in battle against disbelievers for the cause of Allah, with specific rulings for burial.
كفن (kafan): The shroud in which the deceased is buried. For the martyr, his own clothes serve as the shroud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the martyr will need them for warmth in the grave.
B) Because the martyr will appear on the Day of Judgment with his blood-stained clothes and argue for martyrdom.
C) Because the clothes are considered najis and must be removed.
D) Because the Prophet forbade removing any clothes from the slain.

Key Takeaway
The martyr's shroud is his own clothes; only non-shroud items are removed and deficiency is supplemented.

Washing the Martyr Exceptions: Child, Insane, and Those in Janabah
Ruling with proof on exceptional martyr washing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of martyrs that are washed in the Hanafi school and explain the rationale for each exception.

Core Idea
Martyrdom purifies sin, so only those with sin go unwashed; children and the insane have no sin, and those in janabah need ghusl.

In the Hanafi school, martyrs of the battlefield are generally not washed, as their martyrdom is believed to purify them. However, this rule has important exceptions. This lesson explores those exceptions: children, the insane, menstruating and postpartum women, and those in a state of janabah (major ritual impurity). We will examine the rationale and the scriptural proofs that support these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule and Its Basis
Start by recalling that the default ruling is that martyrs are not washed because martyrdom itself purifies. This purification applies to those who have sins to be expiated.
2
List the Exceptional Categories
From the passage, list the five categories that are exceptions: a child (sabi), an insane person (majnun), a menstruating woman (ha'id), a postpartum woman (nufasa'), and one in a state of janabah (junub).
These categories fall into two groups: those without sin (child, insane) and those in a state of ritual impurity.
3
Explain the Rationale for Each Group
For the first group (child, insane): martyrdom purifies only those who have sins; these have no sins, so they remain unpurified. For the second group (ha'id, nufasa', junub): they already have an obligation of ghusl due to their impurity, and martyrdom does not remove that obligation.
Thus, both groups require washing like any ordinary deceased person.
4
Examine the Proofs
Analyze the hadith of Hanzalah: the Prophet said the angels washed him because he was junub. This shows that a junub martyr needs washing. Also review the athar from Hasan al-Basri stating that a junub needs two ghusls: one for janabah and one for death.
These proofs establish that janabah (and by analogy, menstruation and postpartum) necessitates washing even for a martyr.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
This rule is specific to the Hanafi school. Other schools may hold different positions—some wash all martyrs, some wash none. The Hanafi view is a middle position, relying on the specific proofs mentioned.
The dispute is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح : بچہ اور دیوانہ قتل کیا گیا تو انکو نسل دینے کی بنیاد یہ ہے کہ قتل اسکو پاک کرتا ہے جس پر گناہ ہواور بچہ اور دیوانہ پر کوئی گناہ نہیں ہے اس لئے انکو پاک نہیں کرے گا ، اس لئے انکو نسل دیا جائے گا۔ اور حائفہ اور نفساء اور جنبی کو نسل دینے کی بنیاد یہ ہے کہ ان پر غسل فرض ہے اس لئے ان کو نسل دیا جائے گا۔

( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۳۲، في الحب والحائض يموتان ما يصنع بهما، ج ثانی ص ۲۵۹، نمبر ۱۱۰۱۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جنبی اور حائضہ اور نفساء پر دو نسل ہیں ، ایک جنابت کی وجہ سے اور دوسری موت کی وجہ سے۔ اس لئے جنابت کا غسل دیا جائے گا۔
Translation: (977) And he will be washed if he killed a child, an insane person, a menstruating woman, a postpartum woman, or one in a state of janabah. Commentary: The basis for washing the child and the insane is that killing purifies the one who has sin; the child and the insane have no sin, so it will not purify them; therefore they will be washed. And the basis for washing the menstruating woman, postpartum woman, and one in janabah is that ghusl is obligatory upon them, so they will be washed. Evidence: (1) In the hadith: Yahya ibn 'Abbad ibn 'Abdullah narrated ... Hanzalah ibn Abi 'Amir: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Your companion is being washed by the angels. Ask his wife.' She said: 'He left while he was junub upon hearing the call to battle.' The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Therefore the angels washed him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Junub Yustashhad fi al-Ma'rakah, vol. 4, p. 2, no. 6814; Kitab al-Jana'iz; Mustadrak al-Hakim, Dhikr Manaqib Hanzalah ibn 'Abdullah, vol. 3, p. 225, no. 4917). In this hadith, Hanzalah, who was junub, was washed. (2) In this athar, there is mention of two ghusls being obligatory: From al-Hasan: 'When a junub dies, he said: He is given a ghusl for his janabah and a ghusl for death, and similarly his saying concerning the menstruating woman: when she becomes pure and then dies before washing.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab 32, fi al-Junub wa al-Ha'id Yamutan ma Yushna' bihima, vol. 2, p. 259, no. 11017). In this athar, it is that the junub, menstruating woman, and postpartum woman have two ghusls: one due to janabah and the other due to death. Therefore, the ghusl of janabah will be given.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning when a martyr is washed despite the general rule that martyrs are not washed. The matn in the translation indicates that a child (sabi), an insane person (majnun), a menstruating woman (ha'id), a postpartum woman (nufasa'), and one in a state of janabah (junub) are to be washed if killed in battle. The Urdu commentary explains the rationale: martyrdom purifies only the sinner; a child and an insane person have no sin, so their killing does not purify them, hence they must be washed. For those in ritual impurity (ha'id, nufasa', junub), ghusl is already obligatory for their impurity, and martyrdom does not remove that obligation. The proofs: the hadith of Hanzalah (who was junub and the angels washed him) shows that a junub martyr is washed; the athar from Hasan al-Basri states that a junub needs two ghusls: one for janabah and one for death. This establishes the Hanafi rule that in these exceptional cases, the martyr is washed like an ordinary deceased person.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, which remains even after martyrdom.
حائض (ha'id): Menstruating woman; in this context, a woman killed while menstruating.
نفساء (nufasa'): Postpartum woman; one in the period after childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a child martyr washed while an adult martyr is not?
A) Because the child is not considered a real martyr.
B) Because martyrdom purifies only those who have sins; a child has no sins, so it does not purify.
C) Because the child's body is impure.
D) Because the Prophet explicitly ordered washing for children.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires washing for martyrs who are children, insane, menstruating, postpartum, or junub because martyrdom does not purify those without sin or those already in a state of ritual impurity.

Washing the Martyr Who Engaged in Worldly Activities (Irtithath)
Ruling on washing the wounded who engaged in worldly activities after battle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on irtithath, list the ten worldly acts that negate the complete martyr status, and apply the principle to determine whether a deceased must be washed or not.

Core Idea
Worldly benefit after wounding negates martyr status; such a person must be washed like any ordinary deceased.

In the Hanafi madhhab, a person who dies in battle is generally not washed, as he is a martyr. However, if the wounded person survives long enough to engage in any worldly activity, he loses that special status. This passage from our matn lists ten specific actions that constitute 'irtithath'—benefiting from the world after the wound—and establishes that such a person must be washed and prayed over. The proof comes from the practice of Sayyiduna 'Umar, who was washed after he ate and drank following his stabbing.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for martyrs
Recall that a person who dies in battle (shaheed) is not washed, shrouded in his own clothes, and buried. This is the default ruling based on the Prophet's practice.
The principle is based on the hadith: 'Do not wash the martyrs.'
2
Identify the exception: Irtithath
The passage lists ten specific worldly activities that, if performed after being wounded, break the martyr status and require washing. These include eating, drinking, sleeping, medical treatment, passing of one prayer time while conscious, moving from the battlefield for comfort, making a will, buying/selling, excessive speech, and any other conscious worldly benefit.
The list is not exhaustive; any conscious worldly benefit triggers the exception.
3
Analyze the proof from the Companion
The dalil is the action of Sayyiduna 'Umar. After being stabbed, he ate and drank, and subsequently was washed, shrouded, and prayed over. This shows that such worldly actions negate the complete martyr status.
The proof is a qawl sahabi, which is a strong evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Determine the underlying principle
The principle is: complete martyrdom requires immediate death without any conscious worldly engagement. Any worldly benefit after the wound indicates the person was not completely detached from worldly life, so normal funeral rites apply.
The ruling is based on the understanding that martyrdom is a special honor that requires complete sacrifice.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Given a scenario, check if any of the ten acts occurred. If yes, washing is wajib; if no, the person remains a martyr and is not washed. For example, moving to avoid being trampled is not irtithath, but moving for comfort is.
The application requires careful consideration of the intent and nature of the action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۹۷۸) یا جنگ کے ختم ہو جانے کے بعد فائدہ اٹھایا ہو، مثلا ، کھائے پئے یا سوئے، یادوا کرے، یا ہوش و حواس کی حالت میں ایک وقت کی نماز کا وقت گذر جائے ، یا میدان جنگ سے منتقل کیا جائے بشرطیکہ گھوڑے کے روندنے کا خوف نہ ہو، یا وصیت کرے یا خرید و فروخت کرے، یا زیادہ کلام کرے تو ان سب کو نسل دیا جاوے گا۔ تشریح : رث کا معنی ہے زخمی کو میدان جنگ سے منتقل کرنا، یہاں ہے زخم لگنے کے بعد فائدہ اٹھانا۔ یہاں ارتثاث کی • اشکلیں بیان کی ہیں ۔ اصول یہ ہے کہ ظلم کامل ہو تو غسل نہیں دیا جائے گا، اور زخم لگنے کے بعد ہوش وحواس کی حالت میں دنیا سے کسی قسم کا فائدہ اٹھایا تو ظلم کامل نہ رہا اس لئے اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا، او پر فائدہ اٹھانے کی دس صورتیں بیان کی ہیں ۔ ہوش کی حالت میں نماز کا وقت گزر جائے تو اس پر نماز فرض ہو جائے گی ، تو گویا کہ اس نے فائدہ اٹھایا۔ میدان جنگ سے اس لئے زندہ منتقل کیا کہ گھوڑے زخمی کو روند نہ دے تو یہ ارتثاث نہیں ہے، لیکن راحت اور آرام کے لئے زخمی کو میدان سے منتقل کیا تو یہ بھی ارتثاث ہے اس لئے غسل دیا جائے گا۔ باقی صورتیں آسان ہیں۔
وجه : (۱) اس کی دلیل یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عمر بن ميمون في قصة قتل عمر حين طعنه قال فطار العلج بالسكين ذات طرفين لا يمر على احد يمينا ولا شمالا الا طعنه وفى ذلك دلالة على انه قتل بمحدد ثم غسل و كفن وصلى عليه ( سفن سمجھتی ، باب الرنث الخ، ج رابع ص ۲۵ نمبر ۶۸۲۰ ) اس اثر میں حضرت عمر کوزخم لگنے کے بعد انہوں نے کھایا پیا ہے، اس لئے ان کو غسل دیا گیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زخم لگنے کے بعد جس نے دنیا سے فائدہ اٹھایا اس کو نسل
Translation: (978) Or if he benefited after the end of the battle, such as eating, drinking, sleeping, treating, or the time for one prayer passed while he was conscious, or he was moved from the battlefield not out of fear of being trampled by horses, or he made a will, or bought and sold, or spoke too much—then all these will be washed. Commentary: 'Rath' means to move the wounded from the battlefield; here it means benefiting after being wounded. The forms of irtithath are mentioned. The principle is: if the martyrdom is complete, he will not be washed; if after being wounded he benefited from the world in a conscious state, then the martyrdom is not complete, so he will be washed. There are ten forms of benefiting. If the time for prayer passes while he is conscious, prayer becomes obligatory on him, so he has benefited. If he is moved from the battlefield so that horses do not trample him, it is not irtithath; but if moved for comfort and rest, it is irtithath and thus he will be washed. The remaining forms are easier. Evidence: (1) The proof is this saying of a Companion: From 'Umar ibn Maymun in the story of the killing of 'Umar when he was stabbed: 'The fire worshipper flew with the double-edged knife, not passing anyone left or right without stabbing him.' Therein is evidence that he was killed by a sharp instrument, then he was washed, shrouded, and prayed over. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Rith ..., vol. 4, p. 25, no. 6820). In this athar, 'Umar ate and drank after being wounded, so he was washed. Thus it is known that whoever benefits from the world after being wounded will be washed.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning irtithath—when a wounded person survives the battle and engages in worldly actions, he loses the status of a complete martyr and must be washed. The matn lists ten scenarios: eating, drinking, sleeping, receiving medical treatment, the passing of one prayer time while conscious, being moved from the battlefield for comfort (not to avoid trampling), making a will, buying/selling, and excessive speech. The principle is that martyrdom requires complete detachment from worldly benefit after the wound; any conscious worldly engagement indicates incomplete martyrdom. The proof is the story of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) who, after being stabbed, ate and drank, and consequently was washed, shrouded, and prayed over. This shows that the general rule of not washing martyrs does not apply to those who exhibit irtithath. The Hanafi madhhab emphasizes that the complete martyr is one who dies immediately without any worldly action; otherwise, the normal funeral rites apply.

Key Terms
ارتثاث (irtithāth): The state of a wounded person who survives the battle and engages in worldly benefits, thus losing the special martyr status.
رث (rath): Moving the wounded from the battlefield; in this context, benefiting after being wounded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wounded person is moved from the battlefield to avoid being trampled by horses, is this considered irtithath requiring washing?
A) Yes, because any movement from the battlefield constitutes irtithath.
B) No, because it was done to save his life, not for worldly benefit.
C) Yes, if he is moved after a prayer time passes.
D) No, because he was unconscious.

Key Takeaway
A wounded person who engages in any worldly activity after the battle must be washed, as he has forfeited the complete martyr status.

Ruling on Irtithath: When a Wounded Fighter Must Be Washed
Ruling and proofs for when a wounded fighter receives ghusl after taking worldly benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on irtithath, list the actions that constitute irtithath, and identify the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
A martyr who takes any worldly benefit after his wound must be washed; only the perfect martyr escapes ghusl.

In the Hanafi school, not every martyr is buried without washing. The key distinction is irtithath — taking benefit after the battle. This lesson examines the ruling and the evidence from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions, showing how a fighter's actions after being wounded determine whether he retains the status of a complete martyr.

Guided Path
1
Define irtithath
Understand that irtithath means taking worldly benefit after being wounded in battle. This removes the status of perfect martyr.
Literal: transferring a wounded person from the battlefield; figurative: any worldly benefit.
2
List the ten actions of irtithath
Identify each action mentioned in the text: eating, drinking, sleeping, treatment, passing of a prayer time while conscious, moving from battlefield (unless for fear of horses), making a will, buying, selling, speaking much.
The common element is conscious, worldly benefit.
3
State the ruling
If any of these actions occur, the fighter is no longer a perfect martyr; ghusl becomes wajib.
The opposite: if no such action, the fighter is a perfect martyr and is buried without ghusl.
4
Analyze the primary proof (Hanzalah hadith)
The hadith of Hanzalah al-Ghasil shows that even a martyr in janabah was washed by angels. This indicates that a martyr who had a worldly condition (janabah) is washed, analogous to any worldly benefit.
Hanzalah was martyred while in janabah; the Prophet ordered his washing by angels, proving that martyrdom does not override the need for ghusl if a worldly state exists.
5
Supporting proofs from the Companions and scholars
The text cites the example of Umar (he ate and drank after being stabbed, so he was washed), and reports from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that a fighter with any life (ramaq) is washed like an ordinary deceased.
These strengthen the rule that any worldly benefit after wounding triggers ghusl.
